O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, three sons, I have fulfilled this book that is behind the science of medicine, the fulfillment of it, and made the end through its exposures and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I have fulfilled this with the method, which is from the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is troubled in our region and is all overturned in every way, if it is perished by the science and knowledge, and there is nothing more to do than the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and ignorance, and the intentions are closed and science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems that I could bring it back to life by assembling the order of this cauterization according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will assemble the forms of the burners of cauterization, and other instruments of the work with the alignment of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is their craft.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no one finds skilled hands in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters this to surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he sees the judgment of the bones, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of the parts, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, and limbs, and the number of joints, and the movement and rest of the limbs, and also of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Ypocras says that without the non with the evil is not worth, and with the will is little; and at the same time in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the introduction of this book, we say that who are not known of things said, if he tries it may be in error and may hurt men; therefore I have often seen these who enter into this science and then abandon it and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I see a madman who cuts off the testicles of a man or the neck of a woman, and cuts the arteries near the neck; because so much blood issues out that the woman dies in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And if another man's wound is infected by a thorn, and the thorn is large; if it is removed with the bladder of the uterus, and he died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to treat the wound, and I see the position of the patient and the size of the piercing, and if it was not cut well, he died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And if another man's leg was treated by our king who had a broken bone, and with the splint it was plained; and the patient complained of ignorance, and pulled out the break at the plaint as soon as possible, and did not leave any pain in the plaint, and left it to heal; and the command was given that it should not be removed; and later, when the leg was completely frozen and the toe, it came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called to come to him, and I hurried to come uncover the leg; and when I dislocated it if it was in pain and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the ways of the corruption were already confirmed or member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease by the member as long as the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another miracle that I will fall into enchantment and then inflamed by the malice of his ladyship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when he is free of melancholic umor, only a touch of iron can be applied if it is not in the part of the leg that can restore what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	For this reason, trembling hands, you should know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions: it is to know, how or it has risk in other dispositions; and I will show each page of this book where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, trembling hands, you should know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions: it is to know, how or it has risk in other dispositions; and I will show each page of this book where there is fear and risk. And take your weapons in hand, and take your remedies lightly and firmly, and use the best way if for the grace of God you come to salvation and be healthy; and let the unpleasant diseases of grief be healed; and keep your arms from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to another of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	1. Galen's students often ignore his advice: "Do not take medicine for illness, lest you become a foolish fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	2. I have read this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	3. The first chapter is about fire cauteries and cauteries with medicinal heat, and it is ordered by the chief up to the feet; and the forms of strangulations, and of strangulating instruments, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	4. The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and ventouses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it is ordered and the forms of strangulations.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered by the loins' joints, and the forms of the muscles.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	However, if we remember our work, it is necessary that I give the quality of the aid and not harm to each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and not harming, is the longest speech and the most subtle science and the secret remedy; and for this they speak of more cases, and agree to it; and they do not complain much about their words, because I insist on longevity.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally with all complexions or matters, however: it is to know the following complexions: hot complexions with matter, and dry complexions with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions, all matter is determined and they say that cauterization is great help; the other says the opposite: that cauterization is only good for disease that comes from choler and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of hot fire is hot, and it should not be cured by hot disease from choler, or by drought; and they say those who say the opposite that cauterization helps greatly with hot disease that comes from men's courage.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you perceive the heart of the patient and its moisture at the complexion of hot fire, you release the heart's force.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I concur with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it at any time by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all paths, no one intermeddles with it but he who has experienced it and knows by long practice the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their relapses and their spasm; others' complexions we do not know, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And they make it resemble and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Understand, children, that cauterization resembles fire if it is a secret of the cure, and more beneficial than the ardent medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the flesh is simple, and only comes to harm when it is cooked, and does not harm other parts.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The ardent medicines come from one part to another by removing, and bring diseases of grief to the healthy state; and by chance, the patient's flesh may be too high and too beneficial in substance, and does not cause harm, if it has no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	1. And I found this in my experiments and through the service and study I have given to the art, and it is true; and for this I apologize for the length of the speech, because I only want to tell you the secret that is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, as it cures diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says by demonstrating; and you should receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	1. Know, my son, that the cauteries should be made according to their strength, and they are called first aid.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	1. I say that cauterization is useful in all strengths, because the wounds that are not healing are misplaced by the help of cauterization; and furthermore, if the cauterization is for necessary pains and hastens that cannot wait for the strength that greatest malice does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	1. And never think that the patient is cured once the hair is cut, for the disease that is healed by cauterization has no return; and he says thus, but it is not so if one takes care, because cauterization is only a medicine that dries the complexion and dries the humors that cause pain, and is as good as medicine to hasten one's valor, and for one's virtue in their work and their ladyship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	2. And it is possible that the disease returns no more according to the complexion of the patient and the humors of the disease and their virtue; and they are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meat and such things, if not cauterization is administered to him or he has little superfluity and moisture, as with cauterization for pain, and the such things, and part of the pain does not return; but this is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	For many people do not understand why cauterization is called a branch of medicine, and this is seen; but they only believe that cauterization is after medicine, but we understand it is false, and it is cauterization of medicine because when we administer remedies for any disease and they do not work, then we use cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Indeed, cauterization is considered a branch of medicine, but not according to the attention of the foolish.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that an instrument of gold was as deadly as one of iron, and they said this because of the quality of the gold and the highness of its substance; and they said that the use of gold in cauterization does not make any poison, but it is true because I have experienced it and found that it is true in some people; and gold cauterization is as deadly as iron cauterization, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And all that while you are heating the instrument of gold, you do not know when it is heated by the color of the gold, and it has cooled down too much; if it is heated too much, it will cause burns; and then it is enough to prevent it.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that is why we use fire cauterization in our work, as we have already mentioned.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter of the lighter pieces, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	oil cauterization is used for moisture and cold in the cheek, and in it is done by the cause of a disease called "soda", and by the cause of many humors that descend from the head as ears, eyes, and numerous dreams and toothache and throat pain, and also for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and semblances of disease.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is if the patient is purged by medicine that changes the hair III nuis or IIII, according to which virtues and age and habit of the patient can endure; then repeat the dose of the patient's medicine.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then place the root of your palm between the roots of his nails on his two fingers; and if you see your two means, he bleeds and washes the cauterization called "olivare", which is formed:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And he places it on the skin with ink, and descends and gently pulls your hand down and twists, then loosens your hand slightly, and rewards the skin if you see the bone I small; and if you do not see it, if the cauterization resumes as you see the bone as I told you; then take a piece of cloth, and wet and soft cotton, and place on the skin, and let it be three jaws; then make it with moistened gauze, until the burn is set; then cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", as long as it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said to the elder that the older the wound is, the more it festers; and for this, help is needed.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that the fire cautery should be so tight that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned of the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the fire cautery should be so tight that it pushes into the bone, and if it is too hard, it can break the bone as wide as a needle's eye that women put in their fingers because the humors come out outside; and it should be left for a long time over the wound; after that, it should be treated and sewn.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	1. These two methods of cauterization do not seem less effective in total, regardless of whether any man has fear or not; and I believe that I should leave them; for the head of the shoulder is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have experienced in other parts; and even when the patient's strength is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems more effective and painless to me, and therefore I use it in this way.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	2. of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	3. When the whole head is in chronic pain and lasts a long time, if it must use the drugs called "cochie" and purges of the head and oils and plasters; and if it is made the cauterization we have mentioned before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	The head of the patient is of great nature and cannot be too tight; therefore, the cauterization is done on that which we have previously described as a cauterization.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After the cauterization is done on each corne of the head, as we have previously described, and then the cauterization is done on the leu which is called "the nails"; and these are those that are put in a ventsoule; and hold your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will explain further; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the corne be more subtle than those of the head's nails, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere de feu comande au
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in one part of the body, and it spreads to the whole body, and the head is purged with medicines, and other treatments have been done as I mentioned in the division of diseases, but none of them help: therefore, I perform cauterization in two ways, that is, with hot medicine and with iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	If you apply hot medicine with a piece of alum, and it burns and scars the skin and causes it to heal in two or three days, then you make an opening in the temple where the pain is located, so that you can put the piece of alum back on; and when it is put back on, if the patient holds it well and leaves it for twelve hours, then the piece of alum is removed and the wound is dressed with a piece of linen for two or three days; then the opening is made as deep as possible until the wound is completely healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of inflammation, once it is healed; and if you see that there are any other remedies as harmful as those I have written or treated with dangerous drugs.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron burn, if it follows this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron burner, and its shape is as follows:

de la cure de fistule par cautere	The treatment of fistulas by cauterization

Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then continue the cauterization once more, and if you have the skill, and leave it for three days; then place cotton wool on the bure, and apply the desiccating ointment as long as it is dry, and when forty days have passed and it is dry, if you apply an acidic corrosive medicine to the bone until it is exposed; and follow according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing fistulas that no ancient one mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and then put in the forceps of coi. After that, there is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the size of a .з.; and hold your hand with the forceps closed, and do not move the patient until the plasters have melted and stuck to their oil; and it is necessary to put on the oil in cotton wool or in abin d'uefz or in awes: the plaster if it is large enough for the fistula, and it is healthy for the health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the fire cautery we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer antibiotics to the newborn, and to bring the fistula back to its own body according to what is appropriate for the specific wound.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are cracks in the lips that are called "cracks," and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks according to what we have described in divisions, and the patient does not improve, then use a small fire cautery according to this form:

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the gall
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the root of the gallbladder or uterus, or bladder, or roots of teeth, and it becomes inflamed and forms a fistule; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit well: therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize according to the size of the fistule; after the bolt or rupture of the fistule, and hold your hand until the fire comes from the fire, and when it goes out; and make once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, as long as it is healthy; and if it is cured once, that is good; and if not, then it is necessary to reveal the lew and open the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines and it does not work, then put a piece of cloth soaked in warm water on your mouth; afterwards, scrape the cavity that was made, and put the teeth back together as best as you can, and hold your hand tightly so that the patient feels the pain coming from the root of the tooth; afterwards, gently release your hand and continue the cavity according to your will; afterwards, fill the mouth with warm salt water and rinse it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gum becomes soft and restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from coldness, or if there is coldness or to see, and the remedies of medicine are not effective, then it is necessary to have a master in cauterization in two ways: cauterization with a bore and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with a bore if it is such that you burn the hair of a sheep, and the end in a iron or copper nail; then take cotton and wrap around the point of a pin, and make the burned thread on the painful tooth, and hold as long as it is cold; and often I do this until the virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton in the burned thread are charred, and put on the painful tooth, and put on a copper nail as much as the flesh is on the chew of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	1. When the fire cautery is used, if it is large enough to bite on a piece of iron or gold, and it is thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, and form it after it, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often because the pain will be eased for either the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	2. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with hot water in the pressure of this cautery, and then releases it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	I make a cut of the part you want, according to what you can bear; and this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	of scrophules
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are wet and cold, and do not respond to digestion with medicines, then rinse the knife blade after it comes out of the form, and make two openings for the fumes to exit from the other side; and place the knife blade on the abscess once, or as it suits you, until it reaches the point of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, then make the knife according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in for three days; and wrap it with soft cloth as much as the wound allows, after curing the wound and the fleas as much as it is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the chain:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture reaches the cold chamber, and at the same time when this comes from a cold complexion, it is necessary that the patient be treated first with soluble medicines; after which I perform a fire cautery at the root of the throat, and make sure you do not go too far into the throat, and do not burn the skin but only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards I perform another cautery at the joint of the shoulder, and it is called "clavicle" as we have mentioned before; and treat the limb as we have mentioned before until it is healthy.
de la toust	Of the whole
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the parts of the body are affected by cold damp, and the patient has no fever and is weak, and the disease is chronic, then make cauterizations on the strongest parts of the body as desired; and the other cauterization is made between the second and third toes; and that cauterization called "clavicle" is according to the form given earlier.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains. For this reason, I made three burns on the nail of the big toe due to the quantity of a dose, at all the cauterization points, and two burns on the sides of the two toes so that the cauterizations are at three angles, and there should be space between them as they will produce sweat when they grow hair; and they should be like this so that they do not prick the two parts of the nail, and the figure of the cauterizations should be according to this form in a straight line.

dou cautere de pleuresin	A cautery of tears
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make of tears a cauterization, and in this manner: take an aristolochia root long, the longest you can find, and let it be dry and as large and long as your two; and rub it in oil, and take it to the fire and burn the cautery between the force and the col, and make two punctures as you descend on the side that is bare of the beard; and make two punctures between the fifth costa and the seventh, descending down from the shoulder; and make a puncture in the pis, and the other in the stomach, and in between the spines, and in the two pis that are defending the cautery between the spines; and do not press too hard with your hand, as you would smell.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no ancient one has ever heard of anyone using a fire cautery like this, and they thrust it between the ribs, as soon as it reaches the abscess; and then there is great pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, pain or the patient's death now occurs, or a fistula comes which cannot be saved.
de la mice	of the mouse.

de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for dropsy, for it is done in the way called "asclepytic".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur. Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.
