Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient comes to the abscess with gangrene, if the cure uses drying substances as long as he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of paper fibers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper fibers are grown artificially other than nature, and are woven, if they harm the eyes, and cause diseases such as tears and mucus of paper and albugine, until it is caused by the destruction of the hairs; and the cure follows four methods: either by burning together with fire, or by medicine according to what is in front of or in the chapter of cauterization, and is made by cutting and stitching or by pins, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient's arm in your mouth, then turn the paper around in your left hand; if it turns, it is good; if not, then insert an awl into all the threads of the filament; and let the edge of the paper or the hair grow from the edges of these hairs, and pull the thread through all the paper, turning it at the raseur; then cut off the part of the paper that is loose, adjusting the hairs evenly, all around the wound, from the largest to the smallest; then withdraw the thread, and put a small piece of cloth and fabric on the paper, then sew a figure on the paper as if it were the bow of a ship, like the fiddle of a mirror, and then it should be according to the quantity that you see rising the paper that is described as such.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If a part of the body that requires treatment has a large amount of paper according to its condition, then take all the threads from the lines you have written, and begin with the largest loop as possible; and so one of the fringes near the natural hair growth in lengthening of a root, then pull out the hair at that angle, then scrape it off completely; then sew the two lips together at an eyelet of a fine thread, and draw out the suture, and make air to the superfluity of threads at the two corners of anything gluant, if you see this done; and if not, then leave the stitch and the threads until three or four; then cure the wound with the stitch of things that are dry and constricting, for the paper relaxes from the pain of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is dead (as they say the ancients), and it is over for good if not done another way: and if another way: then see the paper as a figure that is as large as the fur of the marten, as we have seen, at three o'clock in the evening according to this form:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then come those who overpower with equal force according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	Then come those who overpower with equal force according to the form that is here: If you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not even, then take a needle or a thread, and pull it through; and take another thread of about the same length as the great one, and the small one, and assemble them between your two hands correctly; then gently press with your hand, and gently sew all the edges where you have sutured, and treat the wound as much as possible; and if an abscess comes to your incision, so that it is relieved by cerotte and semblance of pain; and never once has the hair of the paper been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The patient with rabies is treated as follows: and you will convert the paper according to this form, and then make the snakes according to what I have said, and they are tied as tightly as the paper and the threads are long; and cope as the heads of the parts you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly over the paper of the oil, and draw the snakes from the formed parts; and leave no others, and the leather that is stretched will die and turn black and rot, as long as it is on it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the force is too great, then the treatment will be as follows: and when the wound is healed and the paper is lifted, and no more hair will be tied; and this is the form of the snakes you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	1. The first step is to make an incision as small as possible with a fine needle, and then thread a thin silk filament; then assemble the ends gently and make sure they are even; then cut the other silk filament as short as possible, and tie off the ends; then place the patient's head in your hand; and if the dislocation is not corrected, it may be due to the subtlety of the incision and the filaments; then cut all the filaments at the root of the hair, and trace them on paper as you pull out the natural hair; then pull out the hair until you reach the end of the filament, and cut it if there is one or two or three or more; then pull out your hand as the hair comes out with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	When the fur is shaved, it is treated and the hairs do not grow back with it, if you are careful with the shaving and do not pull the hair too hard, until the fur comes out in patches and you see it through the oil; then if you pull the hair and leave the oil alone for two or three days, and the fur grows back in its place and the hair is pulled out, and if the fur is short, it is accompanied by one long hair from the cheekbones, and it is cut with that which you leave it, until it is elongated and then it is tied.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oil's fat
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or oil comes, it happens in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from wounds, or cuts, or burns, and in similar ways.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to heal it is to cut out the sore, and cleanse the lips, and put on lint, and leave it as long as it remains healthy; and nothing else is needed in the cure of it for things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease may become worse than the first; but it works things that are softening, like fenugreek; and the rose of Aquafia or Althea and the linen seed, when cooked and mixed with no oil at all, and wrapped in a cloth, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are if you guard that it does not sound like according to the form it was before; and these diseases that we have said are none other than relapses of this disease, unless it revives according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the char that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is called "Axcacritis" truly is called "Axcacritis", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounding and burning and cauterization and things similar; and the sign of the cure in the patient is if you prick with an awl, if it has two threads, and the char in the oil, and it seems clearer on the left side than on the right, so that the threads come in the head of the char; then the char is at rest for all the awl, and the cord is in the large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And if the paper is misaligned, it should be returned to its original position; otherwise, take a ruler and place it in the fold, and make two folds or cut the paper at the edges of the incision you made; then, make sure the angles are aligned so that the figure resembles a letter without the Greek letter "I"; then, adjust the corners according to the amount of fabric used, which is equal to the size of the paper, and tie them with a linen thread; then, apply the remedies we have mentioned for mollifying medicines and plasters, as long as the wound is healing.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	When the disease comes from frost or cold or burn, if it comes that you cut a flat piece of paper to remove the hairs from the papers, and according to what is before; then draw between the two legs of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is different in shape, and the skilled masters arrange everything according to what comes back to its natural figure; and the patient himself, according to what is needed for the cut and excision in other positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	I should have used paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this cauterization comes into the hands of women in such a way that the paper on it is soaked with white of oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it comes to pass that you cut the point of a razor with the wet paper, and lift it up; and the tweezers are used, as long as you touch what is stuck in the subtle spumona, which is neither too much nor too little, so that the patient can endure either the spumona too much or the oil bleeding; and your incision, which you scrape of that assembled one, lightly, so that the paper reforms according to its natural form; and it becomes healthy for all assembled, and never causes any harm in the sharp oil, and raises it to the sweet oil, and to the hot iron; then put a piece of lin between the paper and the oil, and put on the oil fine flax in an abundance of urine; and afterwards use the collar and other things as long as it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the bone of the elbow
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the bone of the elbow can be: it is nerveless and resembles hard flesh, but another that is not nerveless, but resembles dry, moistened cheese, which when touched with iron and heated causes pain, if it does not; and both resemble this towards the great armor, and grow little by little as it covers all the sight and light and movement of the bone.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision if the patient puts his head in the knife, then he operates on the bone; and soften the paper with your hand, then take the bone with small pincers, and hold it at the end; then take a needle, and insert the horsehair, or the horsehair, or the beef hair, and the strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and the thread enters the bone, and perforate all the needle, and tie the bone with a string and hold it at the end, and scrape all the hair that covers the costeit of the bone which has the prunes and the silk at the chief, then cut off the remaining in the root of the arm at all the subtle and slight forces, and leave the natural or the wound, so that by the incision there comes no tears to the usual; and never has the bone stayed in the skin only, and along, as we have said; then scrape all the spatumile is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And make sure the shaving does not touch the rough skin and break it, and that the pruning is not seen; and after the incision, grease a little of the wool with olive oil, and let it stay overnight; then the care for what must be done until it is healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	1. And if the nail is not nervous, and you do not thrust the needle, and the unguis cannot enter, it is often treated with this appearance of a nail of medicines; and I have seen many times in the division, and if you see it coated, then use olive oil on the light shaving according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	1. And carefully cut the finger, and if you see that it does not become soft and the nail presses in, then distill from your mouth into the oil made of lavender and red collie and clover, and it stops the oil from flowing to the other part; then continue the other incision according to this same work, as long as it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. If nothing is against you in the oil, like a poultice, then apply the poultice and first cure the poultice until it is healthy, then continue the incision as before, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the flesh of the arm appears in the oil at night due to great exertion, and a part of it is not completely affected, and tears do not appear; then it distills into the oil that is red and charcoal-like, which is made by combustion.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the charred wood that was burned
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men have never burned any red charcoal, and they cut the prunel and roll it on papers and tie them together to make a rose of balsam; and if the wound is such that the surgeon places his finger in the patient's mouth, then he cuts the wounds, and takes all the charred wood as possible, and holds it with the force of the hand; then cut the first piece, and take all of it to the razor as close to the end as possible, and make sure that you do not let the oil get into the wound; and the incision is like the one we have said in the incision of the finger and with small forces of coi on the bone, if it forms after this chapter as we have shown; and when the incision is completed and all the char is removed, if you use oil of silk or distilled red charcoal and medicines corrosive, and put it over the oil with a pad of linen, so that it is assured of apotheme chaut; and if it does not cost anything, and the without chaus comes down on you, and you doubt apotheme chaut, if you leave the oil and cure apotheme chaut with things apaisant apotheme chaut; then return to your wound as soon as it is healthy, and then make many charred pieces in the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you heal the care of every weak vein of nature; and of the accidental vein, in fire; and do not thrust your hand into any of these wounds as long as you see that the other limb is in pain of this wound.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If there are red veins that are covered with oil, and they touch the eye and cause pain in all parts.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you should look at is the oil that is present, and if it is red, it is likely that there is no other disease but the oil; therefore, in this way: instruct the patient to place his head on your shoulder, then pull out those veins all over the body according to his wisdom, and let the subtle veins be double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be three types of cuts according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then use your fingers to remove the finer hairs subtly, and let the blood flow afterwards as much as you can see the hairs coming out of the skin; and do not cut the skin with sharp points of the razor blades, and do this operation in the middle of the day before the sun, and be very careful in your operation so that you do not cut the skin more than the hairs; and when you have finished, distill the greener and redder oil into it to corrupt what is coming out of the skin.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot bear to endure all of this in that hour, then apply a plaster on the oil of things that calm the pain of the head, and leave it for as long as the pain is calmed and secured from further injury, then resume according to this manner until it is healthy; and this is the form of the forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the ointment fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called an "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with a cautery and according to the medicine of burning heat as I have previously described, and it is not well healed, then it must be closed, and all the moisture that is in it must be drained until the wound is discovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and darkness, if all the instruments of this kind are not made of one form; then it is called "sharp chief," and should be made firm in the chief, and should not be pointed like a knife as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the head of the corrupt bone, then twist it between your two hands, and press your hand as much as you can to ensure that this corruption is removed; and do this as few times as possible, then restore the bone with medicated extricants.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is seen, and it is hard, and the belly of the bowel is seen, and remains for forty years, and it does not renovate nor become apostatic, and accidents do not occur, then you should be sure that it is healthy; if not, then there is no other engine than to bring the fistula to the neck of the uterus according to this form: and then you should cut through the bone twice by stone and by medicated agues, and when the bone is exposed if it pierces according to this form, and the head of the iron is at third angle, and the fistula is at first angle if you see it so:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	1. Then place the forceps on the bone of the arm, and gently move your hand away from the oil I pocket, then turn it completely until it pierces the bone and feels the pain as if you are holding your hand above your neck; and then restore the dry medicine leg, as I have shown you, and when the char is made and hardened by the neck, if the matter is at the neck, then it is a lighter thing for the malaide.
de l’issue de l’oil	2. of the issue of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. When the wound is fully opened and there is no drainage from the bladder, and the malaide does not become inflamed or swollen, then you must tell the malaide; then close the wound, then put on ventouses or haterel without hurting with sugar, then put on the oil made of acake, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle, and then strain the oil, and apply it to the bandages and drapelz; if the drapelz are too wet, double each one for IV, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the malaide has used; then strain the oil into bands of a hard bendeil, and resume the ventouses without hurting with sugar; then loosen the ventouses and let the oil be strained all night and the next day, and if it is tightened, then you can tighten the liiens amolist; if not, then after the day and the nut, if you see the oil repaired, it is good; if not, then resume the application and the drapelz and the liiens amolist and the ventouses as long as it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Great shock to the eyelid
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a shock comes to the eyelid, it opens wide and produces papers as if they were resin grains, and it is difficult to see; therefore, cover your eyes, the lid is such that you can insert an awl at the root of the part where the eye socket ends, then insert another awl where the double thread of the eyelid is; and perceive, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut off the double thread and take a part of the eyelid with it, and pull it firmly, then remove the awl and put some ointment on a soft cloth in abundance on the wound; and leave it as long as the threads cling to the eyelid, then cure the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never leave the wound uncovered by the eyelid part of a circle of cloth as soon as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the hairs grow too long, then prick them at their base with a sharp needle that comes from the oil, and remove the moisture and descend the hairs, and then pull as much as it is possible to make it safe.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil's bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not more than bowls assembled in the oil, appearing as sharp; and this sharpness is not sharp; and the appearance of the dislocation if you make it so that the patient lies on his side and right side, then take the chief between your hands of II parts, and pull as much as you see the bowl coming to the desus at your hairs; then it should be straight, and the bowl should be clean of the light, and see the patient's things as he was; and if it does not descend, say that it is sharp, and if the bowl descends from the dislocation is not assembled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient's hand in yours, then take a small sponge and wet it with warm water mixed with honey or fenugreek syrup, and continue to moisten until the bow is empty; and when it comes out, let it drip into the warm water mixed with honey or fenugreek syrup, and then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of the waters in the division, and when it is necessary to perceive; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	1. It is necessary that you place the oil between your hands crossed, being in the light of the sun, and let the healthy and tight oil be well mixed; then put the paper of the oil on your left hand so that the hairs are in order, or on your right hand so that the hairs are disordered; then take with your right hand, if the hairs are in order, the instrument called "almagda," or with your left hand if the hairs are disordered; then place the point of the instrument at the edge of the crown through the hair of the oil at the smallest part of the crown, and gently push the instrument called "almagda" with the right hand until it pierces the hair of the oil and feels that almagda is entering the empty space; and it is necessary that the measurement of the almagda hole be at the front of the measurement of the espaice which is at the end of the nose; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal edge, then put the instrument in the eye where it belongs, and press the hole afterwards with another one.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it is inflamed now, if he sees the physician before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, if it becomes inflamed again, open the second vein with the instrument, and when the furrow is clear and it does not move, gently twist your hand around it a few times; then place a warm wet cloth on the area, and wipe away the oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on a thin layer of ointment made from oil, rosewater, and an excess of oil, and apply it with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and we who are of our kin, put on a layer of bread with an excess of oil.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the thread cannot enter the hole because of its hardness, since it has too hard hairs, then you must use an instrument called "alderet" which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And perforate only the conjunctive, and do not cut too much, but make a subtle hole, then insert the thread, as we have said; and at the end of the work, it should be placed in the patient's eye, and it should lie on its side, and it should not move to the right or left, and it should be placed according to its own position; then it is removed from this dark room, and the eyes are closed, and it is shown to see any things, and then it is placed back in the patient's eye after nine days; and it is only necessary to do this in the eye of the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary to remove it because the wound becomes inflamed too quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the dislocation occurs, move your hand in front of the seventh ribs, and address the one who relieves the dislocation; and when you are calmed, remove the eye and put it on your face or cheek to cover any rib, and be careful in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house quickly and convert into your case; and be careful that no disciple should intermarry in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came from the Yrach who told us that in some places it was made for some reason, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in old books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of the cauterization, because those who do not know them well; and they should be properly made:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this matter be made as subtle as possible, and the tail in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the cloth with the needle.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No cloths ever come out or are torn in different ways, and if there are any that seem like scorpions at the mouth of piers; and if it is such or has a char enchanced with fuxe color, and if it is a char souef of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case of those cloths that are souef and not enchanced, it is necessary that you place the patient between your hands facing the sun; and operate on its nostrils, and grease the nails on those cloths, and tear them off; for if you do not hold them steady at the subtle spumous tip of one part, as long as you feel that the char is all dry.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, and you apply all the straights subtly and lightly, if it does not cause any harm; and if it is not too late, or if the wound is large, so that it does not become infected and all the bones are not affected, then cauterize as much as possible and make it stop bleeding until it is no longer oozing and becomes red and inflamed or wet with wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound is not cauterized and moisture comes to the palace, it is a sign of health; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, it means that the bone has been charred in the bone, or that the straights cannot be cut: therefore, it is necessary to tie the end of a piece of linen around it, and make sure that each hand is tied with the thread, and it must be no more than three times the length of the finger; then put the thread through the mouth of the wound, and take it out when it comes out through the nose; and often do this to the child as he grows, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other hand with the mouth that comes through the mouth, and tie them one after the other as we do with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Until you perceive that the child has corrupted the char, then cut off the boy's penis, cleanse the wound, and moisten the boy's penis with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the urethra as before; do this three times or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the char; then place a catheter of platinum some years until it is healthy, and if he has skill in drying herbs, then use it; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the child's head, or when one distills the oils and herbs or medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a candle, and lead it thusly; and if you see, if I make a candle closed, and let the extremity be plain to expel the grease; and have a hand to hold the head while heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	and of the char for the needle.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the head of the needle causes a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large, until it is visible to look at; therefore, it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and all of it, then put the cautery or the burning medicine; and if you delay as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sense: if it does not touch any iron, because it is enchanted, because when you cut it never, if evil comes to the patient; and if the enchantment is on the point, not of dark color, and you see that you can cover it, if you look at the patient and the point without pain, and cure the patient of things that are scarce and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the dislocation is noticed and reduced
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when one of these cartilages continues to cause pain, it is rarely found in any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to look if the wound is fresh at all its base; and then apply two leeches, one after the other, until it is healthy; and if the leeches have drained all the parts of the wound as they become healthy, then assemble the two leeches on a piece of lint or another suitable gauze, and tighten it, and powder it with dragon's blood, and incense it; and then place a piece of the powder on a plaster or another suitable plaster, and leave it until it dries, and then treat the wound as needed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the sewing is as follows: if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the speech of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lips of the speech are often hard and rough, like grains of sand, and smaller and larger; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and every time you take a new piece, and hold them with tweezers and pull each part; then use the lee after the incision of vitriol, as long as it is not stained; and then the lee of the sand, and cure the lee of things dry as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	The first sentence to translate is "de la char des gencives". The
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the char of the girdles is displaced, which is called "albulus"; if you can hold it with your fingers, and the cloth at its root, and leave alone the bow or the sinew; then put on the leather vitriol powder, or other drying and desiccating powders; and if the char returns after the incision, and many times it does, if the cloth second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the estrumens for copes.
des sordens	The second sentence to translate is "des sord
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are assembled at the jaw's end, where the mouth is between the cheeks, harsh and rough ones; and no times is the black and yellow and pointed tooth, as long as corruption comes to the cheek, and it becomes the pointed tooth; if you want to put the tooth between your hands, and its ends are in your holy place, and open the jaws or the harsh ones as long as it does nothing; and then I make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as long as they are turned; and if this is in the first reason, it's good; but if not, then resume in the second day and tooth, as long as you have everything turned; and note that the teeth have different forms of estructions to laugh, according to what the demonstration shows, because the raser that razes the teeth has other forms than those that are shown between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the patient's tooth pain that you delay and do not hurry, because it should not be done; for it is a substance of high value, therefore there is no excuse for haste.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is confined to bed, it is necessary that you be certain of their toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient has passed, and it is necessary that you make sure the tooth is healthy, and drink the mouth rinse; and it will not disappear completely because the patient is still in pain, as long as the tooth is drawn, for we have already wanted to do this for these healthier ones; and when you are certain of the toothache, if you must scrape the tooth all over the gum until you reach the root of all parts; then take your needle or small tweezers in your healthy hand, and place them well so that they are well inserted, and then confirm the tweezers; and make sure the patient's tooth is well in your healthy hand, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the broken tooth with care, and if it does not break, then take none of these forceps and gently pull out each piece from any part, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are felt and extracted, then it is necessary that you fill them with cloth; and if the extraction is done gently with tweezers, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to overturn the genitals to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well advised that you do not break it, and there remains a part, and the patient should return to the physician due to the greater pain of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And make sure you do not harm yourself by following the ignorant practices of those who, with their haste and hardiness, break through the chariot again and again, but never cause any harm to the patient that we have counted; but they bring the patient only once by the agony of this great disease, either due to the roots that they cut, or due to the chariot that they break, just as often as we have wanted; and when the wound is sore, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and salt; and if the dislocation comes, which often happens, if you use vitriol, then it often comes, if you cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the stummers, or the first teeth, are long and wide and thick at the ends, so they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large members if they do not bend when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have sharp edges to hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth is pulled out, if you must put your thumb on the gum soft and wet with barley meal for an hour or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the root is smoothed, pull out the points called "algefri," even if the head seems like a beak of care; and they should be made in the same way as a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of all these pricks, then it comes that you dig the wound all the way to the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", which is a type of palantine, and its shape is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be large and thick if it does not break the skin, and if the root jumps from this, it is good; if not, then you can use all the instruments, depending on the shapes that come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need to use this instrument with two rains, then its shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like large thorns, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. And let it be known that it cannot be broken, and sharp-edged like those of teeth; and others as well, which are not so hard; and the saws most skilled use their own instruments, according to what their work and the disease they demonstrate, for some diseases have no instruments taught by the diversity of bones and hands, or break not due to charred or other bones, or they perforate, if it seeks estruments as I said, and aids with gestures, according to the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	2. And let the bone be large and well held in place, so it does not break, but can hold and set; and then restore the body of medicines suitable to this, and if there is any pus in the bone, and it is small, then all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears to not fit naturally in the mouth, and it is malformed, and similarly in women, if it is necessary to remove it after the tooth, and it is not correct in place, and it cannot be sewn or woven: therefore, the root; and if it is pulled out with the tooth, if it takes this instrument whose form is like the small bite, and should be sharp and hard in the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the grip is small and small in the hands due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be sewn, then it can be sewn, if the ligature of this part is like the form of this instrument:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	The patient should gently lift the beak with their fingers, as little as possible, until it does not move; then, the end should be flat and have no sharp edges, and the tongue should not be broken or the speech corrupted, if the sharp part is even and does not cause the tongue to break or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the beak is lifted.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the beak is lifted by pressure or with forceps, and the patient cannot press on it as they should, and you should treat them with restricting medicines, and that is enough; if they need to be restrained by a golden thread, because the silver threads turn green and putrid, but the gold does not become loose; and the thread should not be too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the bad teeth, as long as you see sensibility in the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering where you left off, and gently and carefully move your hand until it does not move; and if the root of the tooth is accessible, so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then the head of the shoulder is pierced with nails, and they are assembled, and placed between the healthy teeth, and it is put on so that it does not break the tongue; and then it is left as narrow as possible, and if it remains, or the string comes off, if it is tightened by another string; if it remains and serves for all its teeth, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the incisors of the two healthy teeth and the two canines, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is set, if it is reset in its place, again and again, as we have said; and it does not come out squeezed and painful, and never made into a bone-like tooth of a mare, and it is put back in its place or where it failed, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves for all its teeth.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Of the copper wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is the tongue that comes out of the mouth or nature, which is not needed; or by accident of a wound; and the tongue is such that you can open the mouth of the patient, and put his tongue in his mouth, and loosen the tongue; then cut off the nerve as wide as the tongue is displaced from its place, and if it is hard or swollen, and it is due to pain, if the tooth pains, and cut off large on the same side; and make sure the knife does not cut too much, for the artery that is out of place; and when you have done it, if the gum is red and sore, or cold, then put the tongue in a linen tent; and the patient should be tinctured with the saliva every night, so that the patient's mouth does not become dry.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the dislocation occurs again, if it is not set correctly, then the limb is wasted and the cauterization at the slow cauterizing iron, which is boiled in this way; then the treatment of another treatment until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is not seen as red or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, if it is not touched, because it is gangrene; and if it is declining into a blenchor, and it has moisture, if it oozes pus, and it forms a subtle spumous mass, and it delivers from one part and another; and if the limb is not set in its place, if it is set with vitreol broth as much as possible, then return to your place as you trace all the force; then lift the limb from the hip and the ankle, and the treatment of other treatments until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of the mouth's abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes to the mouth's abscesses called "godath," and they are properly the second mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, then keep guard: if they are dislocations of hard matter and color, and not touching metal with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, and not touching metal with iron, then for the evacuation of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will remove it; and if it is a black color with a subtle root, and you have prepared the instrument with copper, but first look at whether the dislocations are quiet and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	1. Therefore, make the patient face the sun, and ensure their head is in its proper position. Then, open their mouth and place the tongue between their fingers, and press the entire instrument against the back of the throat, regardless of whether it is silver or gold, as some say:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	2. If you press the tongue against the entire instrument and see the abscess, then take the tweezers and the needle in the garden, and tear it as far as you can; and take no other thing from the tools, then place the instrument at the end, and it seems to have many forces; and all the parts are sharp, and one part is against another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or of gold:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you have needles, then the form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then, cut from one side and the other part; and when you have cut one of the hairs, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, heat the blade with hot, cold, and dry steam, and if the blood comes out, heat the blade with hot, cold, and dry steam, or if there are boils from ripe pomes cooked, or sores from marjoram, and similar things, until the blade is not stained; then treat it as it is healthy; and never have any other abscesses born in the mouth except the two hairs, if they are cut like the two hairs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a stomachache that was causing her to choke on food; it was a small-sense abscess. She had nearly closed the entire throat, so the woman could not breathe through the clogged channel that was swollen, and could neither drink nor eat, and she died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so large that it had been drained twice through the two incisions.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then removed the entire tumor, and found a large portion of bowel inside; I then removed another piece from the other incision, and pressed on the tongue; after removing the tumor from these abscesses, and taking a sample, only a small amount of pus came out; and then she was able to swallow water and wine, and continued to cut down on the abscess with each passing day; the abscess grew larger and filled the throat that I had sutured, so that it could not swallow anything large; therefore, I closed and cauterized the wound: afterwards, she did not improve; and I left these parts, and only God can do more after me.
de l’uve	Of the uterus
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the uterus is drawn towards the vagina, and it is long and thin, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and round, it is called "uterus".
