Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, you see that the abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, if you copulate; and the one that is round and not long is assembled and not long; and it is bloody or of a dark color or black, if you evacuate the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said, of its chin and gums, that you should place the patient facing the sun, and press the lower lip on the instrument we made note of before; then look into the eye, and remove the teeth as we did in the incision of the two amandras.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, you will grieve the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two amandras, and cure it as soon as it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	If the patient is afraid of pain, then it is necessary that you use engine for the burning of the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way to burn is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your hand, and then presses his tongue on the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of burning, and confuses with sharp, live force; and with this use of the instrument, whether it is too thick or too clear, the form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair or puts medicine in his mouth, as the medicine of a lancet, and inserts the instrument into all the medicine on the eyelid; and the patient is anxious on his chest, if the saliva and the gums are moist with the medicine given, if it does not reach the throat and the jaw, then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the eyelid, as much as you see the pain and the bitter taste of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and pull the instrument out of the cotton through the canal of the eye, as much as the cotton dries on the eyelid; and do this often until the burning is perfect, then leave it to dry, and after four or five hours, if you have skill in reapplying the medicine, if you reapply it, and after the burning of the medicine, wrap the exudate around the eye, with cotton, and clean what is outside the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured of gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This remedy is safer than incision alone. If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calamine, oak bark, sweet gale, chamomile, and rue, and all or some of these herbs in a pot, add water, and boil; and the mixture can be well glued with hard earth, and the pot should have the instrument made as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the ends of the shoulder be put into the patient's mouth as much as the vapor rises up the urethra through the canal, as long as the urethra is closed; after which it often returns, as long as the urethra is dry, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of gout attack, because many things come; and do not do this unless it is at the decline of gout attack.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and put some wax in the corner of the mouth of the patient; for the wax in the mouth does not cause the vapor to grip the mouth, and it is good cure together salute.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat, either with a bone or a fish spine, or nothing at all; if it happens then you must see what you can see, and press the tongue against the instrument at every part of it, so that you see the thing; and if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, it is good to make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it is helped by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of gum, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and then dip it in the sponge and then glutinize it; and when it reaches the stomach, if it does not come out, and then draw it back; and if it does not come out of what we have said, then take the instrument of pluck according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the forceps be placed at the opening if it can enter more lightly into the mouth, and have the head raised; and warn that you should not touch the epigastrium, as all will vie for it, nor should you crowd the bone; and it is best that the surgeon and the instrument are placed, because either may be misplaced; if it is misplaced, or if it is drawn further away from the instrument evenly, as far as it can be.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the throat of the mouth
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is there for medicine when the throat is closed, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not profit, then look at the mouth of the patient to the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the wound, if it has all its thin skin, or if there are small hairs that are worth saving.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth saving, then take a small hair, and bite in the mouth of the patient, then pull or cut off the hair, and do this often.

de squinance	Of the shoulder

de la grosse gorge	Of the large jaw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernias are called "hernias of the neck," and are large hernias in the color of a scarlet, and are more common in women; and they occur in two ways: natural and accidental; or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways: either one is similar to fat people, and the other is similar to hernias that come from the artery; and if there is pain, and it is not necessary to tighten more than the small one that is present, and prove and search throughout the introducer: if you tighten as I am fat, and cannot in any way, if the cope, so as to cop the whole of it, if there is none; and then close well, and cure as much as it is necessary, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	Of the shoulder
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many kinds of us, and I will describe all the appearances; and it is necessary that I make a distinction between the newborn and the issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is calenture and fever, as long as the eruptions have not passed, and it has been accompanied by the pangs; therefore, the fever and calenture rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the newborn there is no calenture or fever or pain, and it contains sweat, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the heart, and begins thus like a glass, and becomes large; and they are according to these two appearances, either gray or moist, and the color is so as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	1. It is necessary, when you come to the patient's care, that you first examine and ask about all the instruments called "entromissoires" according to what their form brings or is said in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	2. The manner of incising abscesses in the body is that you press or add more moisture to the wound than you remove in the abscess, and turn your two hands many times until you see that the swelling has disappeared, then this is according to the size of the abscess; then take out the entromissoire and hold it steady as you lift it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	1. Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	2. But if nothing remains, it returns to us many times; and if a pouch is needed, and it does not grieve, use corrosive poultices on the wound, tighten the wound, and apply soothing ointments for the abscess, and cure other abscesses as much as possible; and if it becomes large, remove the lips of the wound, and cure that which causes pain.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	When the vein is resistant or if you hurry, use your glove made of vitrolite and leave it for II to III hours, until the wound stops bleeding and becomes quiet; then return to the compresses as needed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the prolapsed intestines, which are three kinds: large and misshapen, and small; and there are three types of "albarets," which are called "breb," and one which is called "grande," and there are three types: large, misshapen, and small, to encircle the fistula's openings; they are also like the beaks of gulls, which are counted by their horns, and are of tin, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable than those that are black, to encircle the holes of the fistula; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the prolapse.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu. et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed on the shoulder once and only once, which strengthens the veins, the arteries, and never returns to this great form:

puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then the fat is scorched, and then the wound is dressed with medicine burning pitch, then assemble the lips of the wound to stitch, and heal as long as it is healthy; and if the breasts are leaned towards each other, and are as large as those of women, if they are sewn in the corners of the corners, so that the smaller line contains the larger according to this form, from this line to the line g.; then scorch the skin that is between the lips, and remove the fat, and what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, as long as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not see the wound, or for the decorrection of sanguine, if you fill the wound with soft cotton dressed in corrosive ointment; and leave it as long as it absorbs the remnant and the fat, then heal as long as it is healthy.

de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans. des apostemes des ners	The first sentence to translate is "des apostemes des ners". The translation
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As apostimes come to the artery and vein, they come from nerves when they are too tight or from too much work, and similar things.

des grosses boces pendans	2. of large bowels hanging

quant li boude ist fuer	When the patient is in pain

dou chancre	The translation of "dou chancre

We have said in the division of appearances and signs, and I will say those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that scabs and callosities, when they appear in the wound, are not noticeable by touch, unless it is by a sharp cut.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are in the mouth of the wound can be felt, they are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	1. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold room, then remove the nails from her toes, and cover her roots with powdered medicines restricting blood flow, such as ice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour water over her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she loses consciousness, if you make her drink a decoction of sumac and the juice of grenadine apples, pomegranate seeds, and similar things, and then take flour of barley, mix it with honey and ginger, and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it pains, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make the patient lie down on their back and massage the area without causing pain; then take a cup of the juice of plantain or aloe vera with wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, if you cleanse the wound with ointment until it is healthy; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles the spine of a chestnut, if it works as I have said, then you cleanse it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Of the abscesses of the gums
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the gums, such as chancre and gum abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, and ulcers, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is necessary that in this treatment I deal with the gum abscess that comes in the gums, which is not different from other abscesses; and if you see the sign of the gum abscess, if you know how to see the sign, look to see if the abscess is red at the beginning of its coming, and with chill and fever, and if it becomes red you will see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	1. Nevertheless, do not force the bone, but make him endure as long as the pain is appeased; then place the patient on the bed, and have two pillows under his head, and support his back and assemble his limbs as they fit the leg; let his testicles be expanded, and put his hands on his knees, and hold them well with a belt; then turn his face towards the left side, and insert the instrument into the mouth of the woman, after which comes the form; it is necessary that when you see him inserting the instrument, you fix the first end so as to know the fit of the woman, so that what comes through the instrument does not exceed what it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if they are larger, it is necessary to cover the fit of the woman with cloths, so that the patient is not grieved; and it is necessary that he place the instrument's handle at the end, and draw the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the suture is open and it is held in the hand, if it fits over the head, at the spinal marrow; and when the wound is seen, if it is necessary to put in the wound tented with softened ointment of rose oil or green oil; then place the tent for the wound at the edge of the marriage, and place it above the marriage and on the clean, softened cut with cool or warm ointment until the wound is cured; then the doctor after two days of treatment as often as necessary until it is healthy; and never raise the marriage and wound with a cloth soaked in cool or mint oil and aristocratic plants that are long-lasting. Then continue the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	When the wound is dressed in the marriage, if it comes that you must not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Labor is first in the dance when the woman knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see her pressing against the bed, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore help the child to be born; and then you should know that these children are according to the natural figure, and are from your own body, and the second one with it; and when you see these signs, if it comes to press gently on her belly, so that the child is soon born; for when he descends from his head, if it is with the second one, and is monied by good hygiene, and the other who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For there is no time that it comes out of its socket, and it comes out of the chest or shoulder, and the hands, or it comes out of the belly or stomach, and it is converted by chance at his collarbone, and through other harmful figures; if it is skilled in the dance that it is wise and subtle in these things, and it warns against error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures on how to help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child is born naturally, and the woman gives birth painfully, and his virtues are weak, if I sit him on a stool or the women hold him, and I anoint his body with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then I dance between his two little spatulums, which is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	1. and then take the second one, and cut along the nail until the moisture that is in it is removed; and then press the belly of the woman as much as the children descend, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to close the woman's muscles with olive oil; then apply and stitch it, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if now the children are born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	2. And if the hands come out further, then it is necessary to gently bend them a little at a time; and if they do not enter, then the woman should sit on the bed, and lift her feet to the top; then lower the bed on the ground, and tie it to the woman, so that she does not fall while standing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the children are dead, then cut off the hands at the joint that is before you, and take out the child, and reset it as accurately as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child with its feet

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner to all the subsequent ones.

Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is said that twins are born many times, and never at three or four; and this is a very strange thing, and has not happened.

de l’enfant mort	The phrase "de l'enfant mort" translates to "of

puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then look for the other shoulder, if you can manage it, when the extractions are equal; and then they should be even when moving from one side to the other, by holding them with both hands, and they should be held tightly, as shown in this example:

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly some children had died, then consulted another and was told that the others would also die, and they did.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought long time, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong attraction with a plaster, and after some days more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised much, for the belly has not any bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted the wound, and with careful hands I took out the bones as much as the woman was better; and the woman saw long time the wound open, and it was a little of blood from the leg; and I do not remember this chapter because when the masters made an strange thing, I thought to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the dislocation back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, which is applied to the limbs; and then it is turned back into its proper position.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Indeed, the corn should be more subtle and restrictive, and should be made of a flat or rounded material; and the mouth should be no wider than one tooth, and the margin of the wood no wider than half a palm and a bit more; and these joints should be firmly held in place, either on one side or the other, half a palm or a bit more; and these joints are turned by the mouth of the dislocation.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	A second form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of flat or square wood; it has two ends, as you see, like the handle of a glove, and they are wide; when you open the marriage, if you hold the woman by the arm and the leg, then adjust the pins together in the marriage, and hold the end of the instrument between your fingers; then operate all the instrument with your hand as you did the nails evenly, according to the amount you see open the mouth of the marriage, until it fits snugly.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all around us and its appearances are multiplied; when we see them, the more we work, the higher the cost for them in quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument because you have not seen it, for its needs are not easily managed.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second child is held in the womb, if you command the midwife to release the hair, and then she pulls it out, and her hands are forced to the mouth and nose; and if she jumps for this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If she does not jump, and I can, and make a pertus or a cough, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the mother, such as garlic, rose, anise, chamomile, calamus, and century plant; all these herbs, or none of them, are cooked or can be brewed with water; then put a basin or cough in the mouth of the mother, and the other hand in the mouth of the child, and hold it until the vapors come out of the child's mouth; then pull it out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second falls quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment she remains without harm, and it is not too late, then command the patient to gently moisten her left hand in oil or musk, and then apply it to the wound, and let the second fall; and when she finds it, grip it firmly but not too tightly, so that the joint does not slip during extraction. But it is necessary to move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes out and is washed, it will be fine.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the joint is very tight, we have said the treatment is to stretch it and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, do not pull too hard; but it is likely that what is in the mouth of the joint, you will tie it to the woman's navel, then apply ointment tetrafarmaçon; if it comes out and is reinserted, and it comes out; but all the same, if it comes out with a bad smell in the stomach and head, and makes the patient sick.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it comes to that, there are confirmed successful fumigations with this: no ancient ones have proved fumigation of cresson and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is made with which they fumigate the woman with the retention of flowers and the secondine if this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a dog, and one places the subtle head in nature, and the wide ones on the fire; and it is the fumigations with charcoal, and the ash as much as it is gray, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to see the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not seen the foundation perceived, but the one who has stirred some subtle facets: if it comes to that, to the dance that he perceives this facet of his own, and not to perceive anything from spumous matter, and leave the plastering that it does not touch; then place on the sick a moistened wine and oil, then the cure of the ointment as much as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not remain, if he puts on a glove of lead, and leaves his hands free, and is quiet when the children see him come into the rooms.

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula with a firm foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from a weak foundation are nodulation, and grow like those that come from the lack of a firm foundation, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodulation is old, it moves, and becomes rough or subtle, and never are these fistulas persistent; they are known by the fact that they are caused by diarrhea or flatulence when the patient has diarrhea, and by chance in some cases.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that puss into the bladder, and into half of the vagina; and they reach the joint of the cervix, and into the womb.

And if you cannot find the fistula at its base, and it is not visible: then you should use a thin needle or a wire in the fistula when it has no twists.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, then use a small tent or a horsehair as a guide, until you feel the tent or the hair in your hand; and if you do not feel it, and there is no emission, wind, or vomiting, as we have said: be careful that it does not perforate; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is present in the vagina or conducted from the urethra, and if the urine jumps out, and cannot be relieved by medicines.

If it is felt at the joint of the clitoris, if it is tight and causes pain in the leg; if it is that it is displaced to the belly, and no medicine can relieve the pain by rubbing; and in these fistulas there is no cure except labor and vanity of proud women who intermeddle in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not a true fistula and not an old one, there is hope for health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient groans at your hands on his back; and he lies on his legs until they are directed to his belly; then make a tent of rain or plank, if it is tortuous, as long as you see or the test comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	When the patient feels pain at the base, if you think it is a dislocation, then it seems that it has been perceived; and if you discover or feel between your toes the sole or the heel, then you should know that it is persian; if it does not straighten with effort, then it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	All wounds can be cured, but it is rare; and if you do not heal, then you should know that it is because the fire cautery is too small for the fistula, as said before; and the wound should be cut all the way through the fistula until it reaches the base; and repeat this two or three times, as you see that these charsets must be arsed, which are like a pen of ostrich; then the cure of soft wounds is to bury them in damp earth, as they are fresh, then the cure of ointment is to anoint and smear with oil.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is in good health, so be it.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If the wound is already infected, it cannot be cured; and if you attempt to enter, do not pierce with a needle that is too small, and cover the wound with a thick layer of cloth or ointment, and you will see the fistula appear at this point where the covering meets; if the cope begins at the opening of the fistula, and ends before the tent, and then cauterize after, as it reaches the end of the tent; it will be delivered from the tent, and will remain; then mold the other charms that seem like a feather's point, and there will be none left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If it does not harm you, and cuts between you and the wound, whether by fire cauterization or medical boil.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauterization involves two things: it is known as the surety of these burned parts, and the closure of blood vessels and the stopping of moisture; then the care of wounds softened in butter or in ointment as long as they do not bite, and it is fit for the burns to be in the wound; then cure the ulcer of sore sores encased in dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healthy and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes suddenly from the side, and it is moved away from the chest, if the wound is large or small, inquire about it.

If you feel the tension, and if it is the skin or face or char, or if it is near to percussing, if not but only a sign of hope and expectation, by applying one of the three methods: if you cauterize as we have said, or if you cope just in front, or if you puff if it has tents and cures as we have mentioned; and do not take too much of a front, that you do not cover the part that holds the fundament, and if necessary, take the exudations by the chosen sense; then the cure, as we have said; by chance if it is healthy, or you remove the covering and mundy then when it is coped from the fundament, or by tent or another appropriately appointed instrument; then make the char that is in the wound as firm as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to prolong the fistula in the part away from the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time are fistulas made in this way: and when you reach the end of the fistula, it is either costive or has a firm hold on the skin, if you take a tent according to this form:

Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you try in all possible ways that you can, it will not work if it is too tight.
