des emorroydes	of the tissues.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	1. Dislocations occur in two ways: either they are caused by the foundation, like resin grains, and they can be small or large, and they can lead to sinus drainage, and they can have one or more, and they weaken the foundation and its base; but those that weaken it the most lack moisture, and they may have a few drops of turquoise or a few drops of blood, and they have the color of corns; and the treatment for those who have weakened the foundation is that you command the patient to spit in the mouth as much as the foundations can be, until they become stronger, and they see the worms; if you hurry, and you can hold them with your fingers, or you keep them in your nails, then tie them at their roots; and if the uncinated ones cannot hold them with their moisture, they should be laid out, or wrapped in cloth, or a piece of camomile, and they are removed from your two hands, then they are tied, and some hot powders that are in the cauterization leeward are applied; or they are cauterized as it is said in the cauterization chapter, for the cure of other cures as much as it is possible; and if the foundations cannot issue, they should be clysterized with clyster mouth and sharp with washing whatever is in the foundation, so that it can issue openly; and if the patient's mouth is not preened, and the filth is strong in the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is that you should preen with your finger or nails, and they are tied, and they are cured as we have said, as much as they are possible, and they do not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If it comes to pass that you intend to sew according to this manner: Take one thread, thread it through an awl, and then pull the thread out and make the awl pierce from another side, and turn the two ends of the other thread around the awl, and if they are wide; and then draw up the thread, then let go of the thread, and draw out the awl, and do this to all the others, and leave the excess of the suture; then put the foundation damp with oil or linseed oil or wax, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to lie down; and then let it stay as long as it is needed, and when it is ready, if the cure for the wound and other cures are needed, until it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	1. "Dou" means "pain" in Old French, so the sentence translates to: "Great pain or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	1. "Maintes fois" means "often", "fiens" means "clots" or "clumps", and "constricting in nature" means that the constriction is causing a problem. So, the sentence translates to: "Often, clots form in the intestine due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is severe, medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. "Si covire" means "if it is necessary", "spatumile" means "a spatula", "ungle" means "an unguent", and "escorce" means "to scrape". So, the sentence translates to: "If it is necessary to use a spatula or an unguent to scrape off the scar, which does not let moisture in; then the treatment should be as follows: when it is soaked, as much as it can hold; and if it cannot be soaked, then the rasping should be done more forcefully than before, until it sings, and it should be burned; then the treatment should be as follows: when it is dry.
dou fremit	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Antor is a small appearance that should appear on the chest, and it moves with every breath; and never does the patient feel it, and it is felt as if they are dying of fremit, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is if you take a horsehair or a feather from a vulture, and place it on the fremit, until the purple circle encircles the fremit entirely; then turn your hand over all the hair until you cover all around the fremit, and put it in front, and excise the fremit at its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, that I make something like a iron or steel needle according to this form, and it is subtle and thin:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	I do not know if you understand, but hold it with both hands and press. And if you see, that the cauterization moves, as it is in front or in this chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the chlister.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time has it been made that silver or archaunt is cauterized, or hammered iron or wire; and no time has it been made of these petty and large stumps, according to those which are in use.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	When it comes to treating children and weak and painful ones, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clitoris is small and large if it is wide, or the belly is shaped in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a deviation or the belly is deformed, as you see, and the clitoris is not perceived; and it is in one of the costals, and in the other, and so is the belly, or it puts medicine from a cow's vessel or from a female's purse, and all parts of the small holes are perceived, and between each hole there must be a thread, then sew in these holes as much as the thread will allow, then assemble the belly like a deer's; and when the medicine is given, if the instrument before a strong thread is attached, then close it; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of urine or something similar, then gently open it; then the midwife applies her hands evenly, as she wishes, then remove the clister, and ease the woman's legs to the parturient, and if the medicine comes out, as much as it can; and if she sleeps a whole night, it will be more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you clisterize due to disease of abdominal pain, and the medicine comes out, if it recurs as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is or fundament, or gangrene, whether it be the clyster also subtle or not; and this is the form of the subtle clyster that is drawn:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division of the cure of wounds; or you will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the place or the wound is made, and how it is made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things made by wounds are made by the piercing of the wound, and the size of the spike and the cuticle, or lance, or dart, or spear, or similar things; or they are made according to the places of the bodies, as a wound that is made at the neck, or at the shoulder, or the breast, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the shoulder, for the remembrance will come to his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, if it is due to stinging of the pierce or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hemorrhage from the head: if the latter becomes healthier of the skull itself if there comes a little blood from the wound, and it is healthy on the opposite part; and avoid the surgeon's fullness with wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become healthier, if the meat is anemic and does not drink wine, and does not eat char, and dresses the wound, if it is apostamed chafed comes, oiled or in vine oil only, or in vine sophitic; and if it has not been apostamed chafed, if it is placed on the wound, it is fresh at all its sanc, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a bit later; and if it is dried out, if it is placed on some griefs, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a spear and its surroundings, and the lips cannot be reassembled by tents, if they can be assembled by stitching, if I say as abdominal wounds, by stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and it can be seen, and holds only by a point, if the cloth; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore the hardness in the leather of the leg, and order the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have or wear leather for nourishment, and it does not reach the bone, if the cloth is loose, and gutters out, then treat it; and if the artery is in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, if you want to stop it, and if you loosen the thread, if the end of a string; and if it does not benefit, if it is cauterized.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	When these wounds are small and simple, if the cure is light: and it is that you put on this powder that has no smell but the one of the herb.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take some incense; burn three parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live chalz, and the fine powder, and apply to the wound, and draw it out as it unites with all its sanc; then close it well, and leave it to dry, if it does not stick; for one does not close the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never has it been done with only chalz, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has not been moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is not healing quickly, then in this case, do not use any of my powder; but use instead some digested ointments or dough made from barley flour, as it grows stronger; then continue with other cures until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then if you remove it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about this later for the major fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the major wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes of the neck and it is simple, then if there is no difference between it and the minor neck wound; but if the wound is of the collarbone or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	1. If it is a nerve, if there is no other engine than leaving the treatment, and nothing to restrict, because the nerves are cold and they withdraw; and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation is with the brain, which is the colder member; but let the medicine be warm, like cold water rinsed, and mixed with rose oil, and rinsed again in cold water, and other piercings according to this method, and moistened things.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if the wound is large, if it is bound with bands, then the treatment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	1. If the wounds are deep and filled with blood, whether at the base or higher up; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs from the wound, if it is stopped, and the lobe, and the cauterization is made; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the jaw, and the guide is kept, as the meat does, if the jaw is under the throat bone, and it is returned according to its natural form; then the dislocation is reduced, and some joints are left, then the treatment of wounds is discarded as soon as it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if it wants to; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are carefully removed, and those that cannot be removed, if they are left as much as the wound allows, and the issue is discharged and cured; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is applied on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If it has in the wound bone and if it has an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or of the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is of the wound of the arrow or of the spear, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at if the wound is mortal; and if it is, then the patient must die; but if it is not mortal, and it is fresh all around the vein, then do not delay in applying the powder at the first hour, and do not tie it with the vein until it stops bleeding, and revive the patient to the chest, and open the mouth; but if there is no ointment, then put cotton in the wound to dry out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three or four hours, or more, until the spasm or trembling of the chest does not occur; and when you see the bones in order, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds with remedies and other remedies, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot be healed, perform the operations that have been made, according to what can be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision of a sword or a knife, and it is simple, or on the back, if the cure that is in front; if it is large, it is bandaged; and if it is small, it is powdered; and if it is infected in the bone, and the pieces are cut off, if the wound allows, and the pus is drained; and if not, let the wound be left to suppurate, if the extractions are removed; and other wounds have other judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of "dou derrompement dou ventre" is "great pain in the stomach".
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no harm to the intestines, and it is difficult to set, this is one of the two methods: either because the size of the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestine is contracted due to inflammation.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is inflamed, handle it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth only, or soak it in cold water and squeeze out the excess, and gently pull on the intestine until it relaxes; and never repeat this action, as it can cause more harm than good.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the flame departing, if the intestine is rough or sharp and inaccurate, it is because of this that the entrance is narrow; and if it cannot enter, then a small wound is made with the instrument on the side of the face; and the first cure is to cut off the tail, which is not necessary at all times but is necessary: and this is the sternum for the fend: if it is cut from the cartilage and does not pierce, and you see this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	When the wound is enlarged and the intestine jumps out, if you put it back in accordance with its natural form in its own place, if you can, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then raise the chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound in the one of the two parts will be higher than the other; and then manage this in large and messy wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you can make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then raise the chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound in the one of the two parts will be higher than the other; and then manage this in large and messy wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I arrived at the intestine after it had been without food for 24 hours and was wounded 15 days ago, and I cared for it and it is now healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And he looked at the wound that was about to die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointments, because I am in II leu where no such thing is found, nor any medicine; and I poured more on the wound twice a day, and the honey from bees as soon as it was healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and pull out the thread from the part that is closest to the end; when it has passed through the eye of the needle, if you have pulled out too much or too little, or if you have pulled it out in another part, then pull it out from the other part of the denuded part; and the stitches will be like those made by the barber, and you leave one time the thread on one side, and take it back on the other, until the stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen calls his own, is not unlike what anyone does, that is, bringing together the two parts naturally and applying one end of a needle to the other in this manner: take a thread or needle point and pierce it into the cloth, then leave the two threads; then turn the thread over and pierce it into the part that corresponds to the eye of the needle on the opposite side; then pierce the other end of the same part with another thread that is on the other side. And this is the better way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	1. If the patient hears this speech and no one testifies to it, then one must sew the belly around the arrows, or at least one; and it should insert one arrow on one part, and the other on the other, in the manner of those that are crooked; and when the flesh is rotten in the belly, if it is more painful than other wounds in the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	2. The judgment of the wound is if it is as bad as the judgment of other wounds: and if you treat the fresh wound with all its strength, unless the gut has been moved, then rejoin the intestine and the colon; then put some powdered charcoal on the wound, and if the gut has been moved, then put any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is bowed; then mend the gut, and be sure of the suture, and the mirror; then cure the wound as you would other wounds, until it is healthy; and if you have no medicine, then put some, as much as it comes out of the bowel, and mix it with vaseline, and rub it on both sides of the wound as often as it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not have another skill in other positions than wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not cause communality as the principal members, then it comes that you lighten it slightly with oil of tamarind or rose oil, and put on the bandages, and remove the sticks; and if there is pain or swelling in the belly, and many times come, if the festered are washed with red wine, and also the swelling comes to the intestine; and the percussion gives lighter relief than the pee.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the knots that are in it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gash falls off the wound, and it is reset as tightly as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it becomes large and turns black, and you see the black limb that has been turned black, because it has veins and arteries; then cut what is in between the ligaments, and put the head of the shoulder down towards the part of the wound that has bowed, until the extraction is aligned with the gash as it falls off, and the plague bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of a bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine ruptures and the wound is small, if it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were mangled or wounded by a lance; and it was the wound on the left side of the stomach, and it was infected and became an abscess, and in it was the egestion and the vomiting; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop refining until it was healthy, and I examined it.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but he had none, but delayed in better arrangements, and drank and ate; and they said to any experimenters that when a small wound is made in the intestine, one must stitch it in this way: take great testes, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the mouth has overturned the lip, if it is drawn into the mouth with the lips, then close the testes, and it will stay if it cannot slip, then make another friction in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely covered; and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	1. If the root of the thorn is in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a thread as fine as a hair from a beast, in this manner: take the root of this thread of intestine that is most clean, and then tie it to the root of this thread I fil of lin subtil thread, then pull the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and untie it at the rupture; and this way of stitching is not worse than according to the course of love and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, if it does not heal or become healthy, then it should be as fine as possible.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula", and at the same time if they are smooth and have a knot.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the truth of nodation, which is hard and painful, or one feels pain, and is as smooth as the feather of an owl; and never in a clear leap, and sometimes thicker; never thin, and sometimes thick; never small, and sometimes large; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that all wounds which are not healed, and do not have char, is only due to one of the eight causes: it is to know, by the small pain or grief, or by malice; or because the pain is too hard and affects the lips, which does not leave any pain; or there are too many bowels; or the matter is impure and of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property in the region is delayed digestion, and delay in health, and disappears by nature; or there are wounds or holes: and I have already shown all these causes and their signs and remedies with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The following sentence to translate: "Or covenant that I make you know the cure for fistula which is made by hand's work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	1. When fistulas appear in all the limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the small intestine, the large intestine, the bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spinal column, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if a part that comes from the proper member of the limb is affected, and it resembles these.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	1. And all fistulas of this kind are of bad fortune, and only labor and ignorance; and if there is no fistula that does not come from the part I have said, and you are a doctor and you see it, then take a needle or iron, if the fistula is straight, as you wish; and if the fistula is bent, then take a fine needle, for the points of the needle do not penetrate well into the bending; and if the fistula is in the hands and you do not want to search for it with needles, then take the pertus that is nearest to it, because the moisture from one pertus makes another, and cleanses it; then you will know if it is bone or nerve, and it is hard to feel with your hand, and ask the patient to tell you how much pain he feels when you press his hand with it, and the leu or the nerve or the artery or the vein, or any of the joints I have mentioned, if the needle according to what I have said, and then the cure will be as I have said; and then the care, when it is healthy, and the fistula is well formed in its right place, if it comes that you close it in the same way that you opened it, as far as you can, then put soft tents in medicine ague, and the bouts you put in until they reach the end of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is exuded from the fount; and then put clean bandages in a healthy girdle, as long as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, if the needle.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	1. If li os do not hinder or the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is discovered, and it has corruption and darkness, if it lasts as long as the corruption remains entire, then the treatment of strange things is done as soon as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and the bowel is straight, as before, you must know that you are not able to do anything: if it is discovered and you wish to be at the root, and all the corruption is removed, then restore the bone; and if it is then healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	2. If the corruption is too deep, that you will not be able to come; if there is no other means than strong nails in nature; and if it has small bones corrupted, and you draw them with hooks, if the instrument is flexible for this, and if there are many bones, do not leave any; and if moisture makes contrary, and it does not cause error or pain, then cope and moisture and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	When you do not operate on the wound within an hour, if you cover it with a poultice made of earth and leave it until the pus is drained from the bones, and then if the bones become softer; and if they are large bones such as those of the thigh or hip, if you only allow the corruption to spread so that the blackness does not extend throughout the bone, then restore the wound; and if a large part of the bone is corrupted and becomes loose from the bone, if it comes out, cover it with earth and put a bandage on it to prevent further corruption, and then treat it as much as possible; and I will tell you about a fistula that came to my leg, so that you can use it as an example and help in your own practice.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The first sentence to translate is: "Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinnt a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; but li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.

And if the bone is broken in no part of the head, then it should be set in this way: take the wires, and draw them up to the top of the head bone; and command that it does not extend further than the first wire; and put another wire larger than the first one on the same side as the first one, and tie it around the char that is out of the bone, and pull the char back towards the bone, so that you can see the corrupted char; and place a bandage or a table under the bone to cover the corrupted char; and set it as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and set it again.

dou feu	The first sentence to translate is "Ou

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	The first sentence to translate is "de l’aposteme de l’ungle". The translation of this sentence
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	The first sentence to translate is "Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe". The translation of this sentence is: "Gangrene is a wound that affects the finger or toe, or sometimes other parts; and when it becomes infected, if it comes to gangrene, and spreads and blisters as far as the root of the finger, and sometimes even further; and then comes the corrosions on the bone, until it causes pain, and the head is large, and the color is dark".
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that is left of the fingernail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is great help when the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the tendon, and it begins to ooze, and blanches, then you must cut off the part of the nail that points the tendon, and burn it at the top, and carefully and lightly cut off the remaining part of the tendon, and apply medicines that are ardent and corrosive to heal all; then the treatment of wounds as long as they are sound.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	1.
