Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron from which the eye is cut if it curves, and does not cut through it, and it is a large gash, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but if it is thick as we have said, then this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the serpent's belly and turns, encased between the hide and the char.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its color, and begins to bleed, as if from the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the wound is open, then you should wrap it with a piece of cloth from one and a half to two inches wide, and leave the end hanging out of the leg, and every time it is not closed, if the wrapping covers the end, and the now, then cut off a part of the cloth and rewrap it, and do not cover the entire root, until it is all out; because if you cover it, it will return to the body, and bring in aposteme and poison or blood, and serious illness; for this reason, it is necessary that it be treated frequently and quickly, and nothing or no one remains or comes out; and there is no time for this wound when it is treated with X fingers or Y, and some hands have come to me, and it was treated with X fingers, and when you wrap it, if blood bubbles or oozes, and the end perforates the skin, then all of it must be cut off; and the matter that is decomposed should be removed from the leg with any medicine porridge without any oil, then the cure should be done like the apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never once in this vein do the hands fail, and at the same time when it opens at the joint of the shoulder, or rather at the shoulder blade, and a fever comes on, and the patient is ill; cure the donques as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the verses that come between leather and char
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "the disease of beef" because it often occurs with blood, and is a small worm that goes between leather and char, and goes up and down the entire body, and sends pain from one member to another as it cuts through the skin or flesh, and causes cramps; and it is caused by some humors, such as snakes, liver, and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes up the body, it reaches the head, and comes to the oil, by chance enters, and destroys the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and drying, if it cannot be helped but when it comes: if you can manage to read the bone of it and the flesh around it well, then cut and remove it, and put it in a vessel, and do not touch it if it is cauterized with fire, as long as it is alive; and the greatest harm it does, if it comes that it is near the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or approaching the oil, if the sorcery forms around it, then cut and remove it; and do it; and it is necessary to use the salve of mundification of liquid medicines for the humors of the body, and avoid foods that are spoiled.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "wanderlust", and is a pain that comes to any part of the body, and then spreads from one part to another; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a female patient, and I saw my arm, and I saw a small flesh in the vein of the shoulder; and afterwards, I saw it rise as if it were a leaf from the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as if living silver when it cuts through the bone; the pain left that arm, and moved to the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, so that it came to the other shoulder; and she told me that she dislocated in reverse along the chest, just as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed to see how it moved from limb to limb, as I have never wanted this disease to happen in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to make sure that the pain was not transferred from one part of the body to another, but I did not want it to be so. And I thought it was because the woman had tightened her corset, and the veins were discovered, and because of this appearance of constraint; but I did not know until then that this was true for those who are delicate, and who have moist veins and recovered voices.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see the disease being cured and the patient feels pain, if it opens as we have said, and if the limbs and bones are not constrained to the body, then cauterize the limb; and if you do not see this at your eyes, if the cure of these that open the constraints is like pills made of herbs, and pills of sassafras, and similar things.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the wounds they cause in the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is that some have large points, and small, and barbed, and sharp; and some have sharp angles, and some have curved, and some have pieces; and one that pierces any member in different ways: either in the principle members it pricks like the brain, liver, spleen, lung, heart, stomach, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. If you see that you are causing the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many ways; and if the sign does not appear soon, and the arrow is not in its place, then the wound will become worse, and it should be treated immediately.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of danger appears when the arrow pierces the bone and makes a hole in the shoulder, and the shock that is felt there is when scotomy, soreness, and dizziness, and fever, and pain and swelling in the limbs, and inflammation of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of the cold; and by chance it does not have nostrils or ears; and by chance it affects the speech and voice; and a sudden jump of the wound, white like pus, resembling a toothache; and if the sign appears to you, if you hold the cure, and extract the arrow if it is not in its place.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it pains or swells is that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it is becoming hard in something firm; and by chance the shoulder becomes as stiff as the leg, and in a short time black blood comes out, and there is cold and cold fever, and convulsion: then the signs of death appear.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the eye that has not been pierced is that there are no signs of swelling from the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the face is pale, and it sighs high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	When the arrowhead is in the shoulder covering, if it is close to the small ribs; and there is great pain and great suffering; and all the members of the arm move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is in the stomach by chance, if it jumps out of the wound nothing digested from the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is in the belly by chance, and it jumps out of the intestine at one point, if there is no hope in the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead is in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes out suddenly, and the patient feels great pain: deadly wounds.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and neck and shoulder and arm and elbow and spine of the back and ribs and muscles and legs, and the seeming member, are excepted according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the flesh or vein, and it is not found, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are making it difficult.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me once a arrow was in my shoulder: I tried to remove it, and it came out from another part of the fat of the ear, and it was easy to remove.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And then there was a case where an arrowhead entered the fat of the oil of ozone and paper of ozone, and the arrowhead was replied to, and it could not reach further than the point towards the other's neck, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, at all times making it light in weight for the ear; the patient was healthy, and never had any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And then there was an arrow in the throat of a Moor, and it was the Arabian arrow with ears: I was the beards, and subtle as much as I saw it, and it was healthy for the Moors.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was a wound in the man's thigh or belly, and I thought he would die; but after three years, if it had not changed its position, I opened the wound, set the bone, and it healed, and there was no accident along the way.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the man has a wound on his thigh or back, and it is infected; and the wound does not heal, and does not follow its natural dispositions, and does not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if another man has a wound in his face, and it is infected; and the wound does not heal, and does not suffer great pain; and there are other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	The patient has a dislocation in the shoulder of the king, who had it for a long time and was slightly depressed on the left side; it was completely recovered after three years.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If you find the wound is tightly closed.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I gently probed it with my finger, and I did not feel anything; it felt pointed and painful on the left side of my ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I put in the leg, because the leg did not swell; but I saw that it was the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I place the burning iron on the wound, and the right-sided pain subsides, as he feels the arrowhead in his shoulder; and he tells me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed the burning iron on the wound, and the wound became overgrown, and I extracted it, and I felt the head of the arrow that had been pushed into the shoulder; then I covered the wound with the burning medicine, as the patient's shoulder appeared visible to me; and it healed well in four months, and then I removed the thorns and the needles that I had inserted, and could not do otherwise; therefore, I continued to refine and invent ways to destroy it, as soon as I had properly inserted the thorns, according to its form as it appears at the end of this chapter, as I healed and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the mirror judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it accordingly, and the wound was soothing to the nose, and the malady was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, if you apply your care according to what I say, because the books cannot make everything appear pure; but the masters of the things make good use of few things, and of what is present and deficient, they do nine kinds of work, and nine instruments, in the descending of things drawn in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the members or they are made from flesh according to the following ways: either by the root or they enter, or by another part; and the one that is thrown by the hand or it enters, is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and it will never be thrown again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if she lets the char be burned through and through, and is not afraid of the issue; then she will get stuck in the bone, and she cannot move if she leaves any joints, and each joint; then she jumps, and if she jumps, if she perceives through all that the lear is slaggy, and then the trai.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and it goes into one of the deep bellies, or any of the accidents I have mentioned to the barber: if it is not drawn out, but left as it is after a few joints, because the arrowhead comes out, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	1. If the dislocation is not in the bone alone, and does not cause any other problems, and there are no previous injuries that have caused damage, then the surgery will be successful.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. If the dislocation is not in its proper place and cannot be moved, then it should be reduced as soon as possible, as I have said before. Then, treat the shoulder until it is healthy again.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	3. If the dislocation cannot be seen, and one tries to feel it, and if it is not in any instrument that can be used for reduction, and if there is no pain or swelling in the shoulder, and the wound is not large, then reduce the shoulder as much as possible until the wound is healed. If the shoulder has visible dislocation, and the ears are held by the dislocation, and the bone is broken at the head of the humerus where you can see it, and then break or crush the ears of the shoulder, as much as you can reduce it, and do it gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not once, if the wound is still bleeding until it is clean, then treat it, for the extraction causes pain.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the dislocation does not move with the blood, if you do not follow what we have said in this chapter; and open the nerve and vein, and make an incision as you please to treat the arrowhead, either slightly or deeply, or firmly or loosely, and set the splint according to the shape of the arrowhead when it was removed, because it is the largest help that can be given, and if you do not, if you do not follow what we show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line translates to: "The arrow that came from another part, or it opens nothing of its own, or the skin is shrunk in a place where one can see or feel it: then it should be cut, as long as the thorns can hold onto it, and then it should be removed: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if your hand turns around rapidly, as soon as it enters the bone, it widens the bone, then it should be pulled out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, if it is left alone, and then the extraction resumes as soon as it is drawn out; and if it is a shaft and it is in the wood, if it is cut off at the end, and if it is a tool and it points towards the hair of the tool, and then it is cut, and if the shaft is hair, and it enters the tool's hair, then the tool is also cut at the point entering, to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrowhead is embedded, then you should cut through the entire arm or the poison is, and if you can, then treat the wound as best as you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrowhead is near the shoulder, abdomen, or lower belly, and it has pierced, and you can reach it, then cut it out; then cover the vein and nerve, and then remove it, and then cleanse the wound as best as you can; and treat it until it is healed.

des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins that are healthy there are XXXI, of which XVI are the largest, which is to say: The two arteries that are after the ears, which are called the "herb-ears"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples apparant; and the veins that are in the two larnices, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is cut at the front; and the vein that is cut at the head of the nose; and the guindises that are or col; and the veins that are in the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the veins that are least below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The first sentence to translate is: "Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The savable part is the vein that is between the auricula and anus, and if it swells; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is the corbule of the opposite side of the chest, and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the other chest; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins like these.

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The patient's vein health is as poor as the face's ancient diseases and migraines, and the quality is if the medicine tightens its neck by twisting, as much as the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fissure", which is shaped like this:

de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the rabbits
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the rabbits' mouths is helped to close in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and fangs of the lips, and pain and throbbing.

des sainies de ventouse	Of ventricles of the brain
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventricles are made of horn, or iron, or silver; and ventilation can be done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This ventilation which is done by cutting is done in two ways: either it is all fire, or hot; and ventilation which is made by cutting and extracting blood is done in twelve different places of the head, where some are all the chief, and others are the collarbone; and the others are in the costal cartilages; and the ventilations of the menton; and the ventilations of the two shoulder blades; and the ventilations of the crupies; and the ventilations of the two arms; and the ventilations of the two legs; and the ventilations of the two ankles; and this ventilation does not touch any veins that are scattered in the flesh, for which reason no harm is done to the patient, as we do with wounds; and it only remains to make sure that it is not all fire or hot, in any disease that comes from repletion, as long as the chest is empty.
