Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If we want to remove a lot of blood, we often return; and if the joint is not precise, if it is too deep, and if the ends are perceived slightly, and for those who have thick skin and hardness, and who have rough edges, you must oil the ventouses aperitif and dissolvent with olive oil: if it is in this way, with olive oil of violet, or with olive of sweet almonds, or with olive of cucurbite seed; and if it is in wine, with oil of parsley, or with thyme, or with chamomile, or other similitude.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take olive oil, or balsam, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the part that is affected by the cold and wide pores, it should not be oiled, but it should be washed after the vinegar rinse, or the cold rinse, or the mushroom rinse, or the cucumbers rinse, or the porcelain rinse, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And that which has sweat, if it rises with oil, or vinegar of myrrh, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluity rise from wine vinegar, or from ague of sweat, or from decoction of anet or chamomile, or from other similar things; and they are not healthier before bathing than after, but rather an hour or two after bathing; and they do not sleep before ventilation, and they must ventilate when they need to and when they are ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are healthy become irritated, and their mouth is too dry and inflamed; then it comes that they need to consume cold things, like green apples and endives and leafy vegetables, and similar things; and they drink punctions, and char of chafing, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	The patient with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup if they are thirsty, and wine that is between vinegar and wine, which is between little and much, and milk, cheese, and pears and pines; and when they start to feel better, they must drink more wine than water; and it is recommended to give some men a triangular or muscle exercise before or after the ventilation, to comfort the main members; and it should be done subtly, but only those who are cold should drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The bellies that are made sore are those that are made sore in the stomach, and in the liver, and rheumatism, and in the stomach and bowels, and in the gallbladder and kidneys, for this member does not suffer much pain in the sides, and only feels it when it draws blood from one part to another, as we do with the breasts when they are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we make ventouses on the stomach and bowels to sweeten the member; and to relieve the pain, whether it has opilliation or piercing, if it is relieved by its own virtue attracting the opilliation, or if it leaves the piercing of the limb, and these ventouses are given empty to suck only; and they are never given together with fire, and never with aqueous tede, as in diseases that cause much crying, and in such a way that one fills the ventouse with hot water, or with water that has been cooked with herbs that are beneficial.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum device administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two large and half palms of width, and has a small pocket on the outside of the mileau I petit pertus, as if to stick an arrow, and has a groove of iron or steel in front so that it does not scratch the patient's member; and in the mileau has a hole for a chain or wire to be inserted, and there are large and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them, because the vacuum devices of children are different from viels, and are thinner than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be placed around the member with this device: take the wax candle or liniment, and insert the vent into the groove that is in the vent, so that it glows at the end of the vent where it does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and you must place it as we have said, if you see that it produces vapor when you look, and if you remove the vent; and take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	1. In the vent that is in the patient who is sick with copious phlegm, without any fever or wheezing, and is only sick when it is clear that it has a cold, and is placed around the member only; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Scissors are not usually used except in parts of the body where small incisions can be made, such as the lips and genitals, and similar places; and in parts where hair is thick, such as the eyebrows and eyelashes, and other parts; and the quality of the scissors depends on whether you can find smooth-skinned goosebumps that are easy to pinch, if you can; and then place a needle in a smooth-skinned goosebump, as long as it is not pregnant, and has nothing in the belly; and then clean the wound and the belly, and then remove the pins, and then place the pins on the smooth-skinned goosebumps; and when they are flat and smooth, and turn red, and put them on, and when they are flat and smooth, and turn red, and put them on, if it is possible to pinch the belly, then it is better to do so.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	1. If not, then raise the leg of the affected side, then the thigh; and if the patient is too ill after the surgery, then soak it in cold water, and wrap it with linen, as long as the wounds are not inflamed; and if the wounds become inflamed, then put on vitrol or galls, and similar things, as long as they are inflamed; or you can cut the leg in half from the knees, and leave them as they are on the leg until they dry out now; and if you have more to do, then take other affected parts.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the wounds do not take on the salve, if you rub the wound with warm oil or thread as much as it will absorb, and then put it on, and as soon as they feel the heat, if you powder some aloe and silk or sand, or dust, now they will stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they deal with fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	I advise you to pay attention to this chapter, as you will not find any examples in the old books, nor letters; and this is why science has been neglected in our land, because I have never found any book on the subject; and I do not know of any, except perhaps through the science of the old books, or through my own study and treatment of the science, and through experiment, and through the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the fractures that have been produced, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of words and chapters or sentences where the meaning is put, and they learn the truth, if those who have experienced it understand and learn this noble art, and learn to teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is any breakage, dislocation, twisting, or tightening, if it comes to any part of the patient's body, nothing should be taken away unless something else is affected, whether it be a wound, or a fracture, or a dislocation; or if it is not very tense, or too loose; and if it is too cold, it means cold drinks, and ice and velvet, and does not drink any wine, nor take in too many thin drinks, and does not fill the veins with blood, as long as there is no doubt of anemia, or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient's condition improves after the first governance he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that cause large swelling, or viscosity, such as wheat cooked in vinegar, and tested, and peeled, and pains in the cheese, and oefz, and fish fresh, and big wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For part of the swelling is regained and more quickly the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that the bones broken and decrops do not regain or heal according to their nature due to the shortening of the limbs, and those who are too soft, like that of small children; but no cure, reset the broken bone with large tenrons that are sawn and joined to the limb as it was before; and do not leave it too long, and for this reason it is necessary to avoid large amounts of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures come in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you all the ways of fracture in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that can be seen and others that cannot, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture is a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own way and instrument for restoration, according to what remembrance comes to the bone; and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by what the hand holds, and is open well by defeat, and some are pressed by the hand; and if it is not twisted or has no pain in the hand, there is no fracture, but it may have twist, or cut, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot manage to move it with your hand alone, but bring the medicine that comes after, and then gently extract it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And examine the fracture that will occur in the wound, and the two parts that are separated. It is now appropriate to put them back together as evenly as possible, unless they are causing pain; and if they cause pain and come out, then it should be left alone until the pain subsides, and then it should be gently placed in its original position and examined to see if the restoration of the bone is lighter than the restoration of the pieces; then it is extracted, as it was done here after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	1. And if in the bone of the foot, if it is broken into two parts, it is hands or fingers, or a part of your hand is small limbs, or two cords, or one cord and your hand; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are adjusted, if you reset with your fingers the additions in their place in the muscles that you please, and keep that by your effort does not cause the surgical wound or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	2. And it feels good to the hand if it seems that it is not well: if it bends beautifully, and does not strain too much, do not press as they do who come by their effort, aposteme chaut and contraction at the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the joint is painful, if the patient keeps it still, neither by day nor by night, nor when turning, nor in any other way, then the joint should be secured so that it does not cause any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, if it is not yet time to reset the joint, then it should be put in proper alignment so that there is no pain; and keep it in place until the injured limb is fully restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I will describe.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	There are various types of fractures, small and large, in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For if it has bitten members, like meat and drinks and similar things: if it comes with entrails of linen and fine threads; and those that are large, like leather and leg: if it comes with a wide and hard ribbon, for the large ribbons embrace all the great member, and draw it evenly, unless it has no tail; then it is lightly wounds, three or four times around the member, and the hand is tightly tied to every part of the ribbon, then go to the end of the fracture and draw it less, that the fracture may slightly move the part of the healthy bone; and soften the ribbon a little and a little, as you please to take a large part of the healthy flesh, then put another ribbon, and turn the wound right side up on the broken bone; then go back to the part opposite the fracture, and draw it gently, not too much nor too little, as we said in the first part of the fracture; then put between the wounds of linen or threads as much as it is even, then tie all with a knot, and then put your good stitches on, if it has not had an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it is inflamed or infected, if you put something soothing on the infected area that stops the inflammation and leaves it undisturbed; then tie your eyes with something like a wide piece of twine, or a rope, or a palm branch, and it should be tied in this manner:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the bandage placed on the wound be larger and broader than the others; and should also be as long as the size of the member; then tie your eyes in the same way as you did in the first part, then tie a thread around it just like you did in the first part, but make sure it is not too tight; the more stretched it is, the less it will be; and the thread should be smooth, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen the works of fools who tie their knots with linen threads, it can cause great harm, because the knot cannot be equal if it is too fine, and only makes it possible that there is less space between each eyelet than a piece of spice.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is relieved by the head of the arrows after the extraction in healthy ones, if they are left without sores of linen, or silk, if it does not freeze.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bandage, and the edges are torn, I will tell you the cure for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And beware that it is not difficult to break all the limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not easy to put on arrows after the first day or seven days, or according to your strength; and in this way the ancient methods of restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists: and that you take flour that is held within the walls of the mills, and mix it with a great deal of beer, and make this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of restoring breaks in other positions, as well as for women and small children, because it is not too hard or too weak.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Other ways of plastering to repair fractures and dislocations and twists: take pumice and linen and oil and Arabian gum and mugate, in equal parts; marble and aloe, in equal parts; alechil in equal parts; and make a powder, and mix with the fat of urine; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and rests the broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Other ways of plastering for twists: take Arabian gum and vinegar, in equal parts; marble and aloe, in equal parts; acacia, in equal parts; arsenic from Armenia, in equal parts; mix well, and cook with water or the fat of urine, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to burn is on joints and bones, and soothes the pain that follows, and reduces the size of the bone: take fresh oil, and the milk en suet and cooked, and put it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not repair, but they are good for soothing inflammation and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to burn that repairs broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth pottery, and bundle them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to burn for the repair of bone fractures and to reduce inflammation.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	1. Take the root of malva, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part; and boil, and strain with wine, and wash the limbs with fresh coriander water, or with cold water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	1. Another way to wash more thoroughly than the first, when the abscess is deep and comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	1. Take the roots of malva, and linseed meal, balm, honey, and sugar, and each part; and boil, and strain with fresh or sweet vinegar, or wine, according to the chill of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not put the broken bone member in a position to restore it as if it were made of clay and oil, and nothing more, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galien says one should put the broken bone member in a position to restore it, using things that are dry and warm, such as mustard and aloe and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to show what is good for the wound and pain: take a piece of raw meat, or the tail of an ox, and a thorn, and sew it, and the limb, and then apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the patient will feel better a little later, and take care not to cause pain or discomfort to the bone of the limb; if it does not improve by hand pressure, and pain comes to the bone, or itching, or swelling, if you hurry, and remove it, and now apply the plaster; then gently dampen a cloth, wet with sea water, dip in cold water, and lift the limb until the itching stops and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moist or oily rosewater, and put on a bandage, as long as you are sure not to have an attack of gangrene; then allow the inflammation in the member to subside, and soothe the pain, and then resume the light touch, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much; and gradually until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the incision is painful and has blood, swelling, and inflammation, and you have skill in plastering and bandaging, if it recurs, as you did at first, do the same.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If you do not see any worsening of the joint for three days or four or five or seven days, and never more than twenty days, as soon as the swelling approaches the chariot; therefore, the restraint is more than before, and the flesh grows larger, as I said earlier; and if you see the joint becoming drier than it should be, do not let the wounds become worse than they can be, and take care to keep the fire hot every time you dress the wound, and do it every day, and put a little oil on the cloth; in this way, you will cut off the fire from the joint, and stop what the flesh does, which makes the joint painful: this is bad, and if it does not improve, I know of no other remedy than to have patience and treat it with due care.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounding
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of wounds are there, and various shapes, and their causes are assigned; for there are wounds made by the impact of a spearpoint, and the whole bone is shattered as if it were wood, like when cut with an axe or saw; and therefore this kind of wound is called "axe-wound".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spear pierces the bone through various senses and is called this kind of wound "absolute"; and these are the wounds of those two great or small gashes.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has an impact that is embedded, or pierced, or from the cut of the wound, or from the cut under the wound, or from other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent fracture, which approaches the tissue that is loose from the bone, or it is placed on the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If the wound is repaired in the bone as subtle as possible, and it is a small cut, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by injury, or by piercing, or by seeming thing, and forces the piece of bone to enter, and it is the same as when they were heating the caustics when they burned the caustics; if it enters the piercing.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more cases where the shoulders have soft bones, like that of a child; and they occur in all these ways of fracture that are light and easily broken, like these; and I will speak to you in his language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we shall examine all the ways of fractures caused by the blows that have been given, and by the crooked one that has been made, and by the char that has been corrupted.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the fracture is known by this, that when one has discovered the bone, and has rubbed around it, if the black fracture is not wide open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close watch on the patient, and if you see no mishap from the surgeon, if it is not like vomiting of bile, and admission of understanding, and extension, and manipulation, and fever, and the wounds turning and reddening, and other signs of more severe cases, if it cannot be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When you first come across the bone, and it is in the shoulder, then it is necessary to open the bone before the fourth month of the mouse, that you may do.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, and you hope to open the bone before the ninth month of the mouse, then the cloth that covers the bone must be rotten, and the accident we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes near the cloth that covers the bone, then it is necessary to sell the cut part: and it is that you press the patient's shoulder with the knife, and open the bone in all the ways you can, and open the wound in its figure more than you can, and if the poison comes out to discover the bone, or if it is a gangrene, then help it as it is necessary, and it is that you fill the joint with oiled powder; and let the wound rest until the poison is calmed and secured against displacement; then begin to open the bone, and it is done according to two ways of incision: one way is when you cut at the narrow end, and it is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I cut it in another, larger piece than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes, some pointed and others wide, and they are sharp, and are made of iron; and they can be lightly carved, without cutting the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, it comes to pass that you perceive it, rather than carving it with tools, as long as you use carving tools with care, and do not force them too far into the bone, and must have a margin or circle around the point that does not pass over the bone; and you must have more tools, if each time you see the bone in your hand according to its thickness, if you have tools for each test; and this is the form of the three ways of carving:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The first line of the translation is: "To check for fracture at the end of the bone, put pressure on the bone, and turn it as much as you can until you feel that the bone is perceived; then remove the pressure a little later, and then do the rest, and cut through the bone's edge that is between the holes, making it as subtly and lightly as possible, and gently, so that you do not touch the brain or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and cut the bone, if the incision covers the entire bone as it is made with an instrument resembling a chisel, but it should be more thin and subtle than the other incision; and if it does not remove any small bones, nor any scales, if the lighter bones are scratched on the extremities; then cure the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of opening is when it is said that the Galenic method is more reliable; and the more forceful, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the fracture is open and exposed, so that once you have removed this part, measure from the center of this incisional lenticular curve, which is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part is cut away in two pieces if the cutting is towards the bone; then, using a small saw, if you lightly touch the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is exposed; if it touches the bone, as it is well known, it causes great pain, and can cause fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	1. If the bone fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only crushed by itself, and it has small pieces, then those rough edges must be covered with something to smooth out the scales, which you should have several quantities of, to accommodate each joint according to its type and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	1. If you use coarse razors first, and then gradually switch to softer ones, and continue doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	1. In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, you must accommodate according to its address; and this is something that cannot be undone by the one who studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	When the scar is discovered, if it is necessary to pregness and drape the wound according to the size of the wound, and oint with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled bandage of II or III, and oint with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first bandage; and do this more lightly than you please, so as not to burn the scar, then apply by other linen, and do not strain it too much, only until the wound is healed; and leave it for I day or II, as long as the swelling is pacified, then remove it, and administer medicines like these: roots of lis, flour of times, powder of incense, aristolochum, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and administer further medicines without mordication; and when the wound is clean, do not leave the ointment or assemble bowels, for if bowels are assembled under the skull, they will cause great pain to the patient; for if something mouth-rending is placed on the wound, it will cause great malice to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents happen to the patient, if no one doubts the sense of the matter, then it is doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no one comes for help but only through medicine that has been given, then it is necessary to have part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, and mix them with soap; then the cure is performed in the ways of cures that are given, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is said that the two parts of the joint are never broken, or only one, because they are bones; and it is in cartilage, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off the small digit or pertus and place it evenly on your index finger, and in the pouch as long as it does not reveal according to its natural figure; and do this lightly, and let the patient feel no pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part of the nail, and cannot reach the toe, then you should place it evenly at the end of a large finger's nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in the second part, then you should redo the first nail, and hurry to restore the first one, if you can; if not, after the ninth or tenth time, when the wound is calmed, then cut off the end of the nail with a blade of linen, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you cut one part, the other will also be cut; and if they are large, they fill the cavities with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restorer would say that one must file the cut edges, and each hour.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that this is well, but they must be filed in the making of bone marrow and powdered milled; then leave the edge, until the bone is cold and the cartilage hardens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And no time is it cut on or the wings of geese in the shoulder of the edges, and if it is too loose and hangs the bracelet, and smokes the drug among; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess is inflamed, it comes to the nose while you work, if it puts on a cloth or cotton that is well greased with oil of rosemary, or in a pot of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, if it puts on ointment made of flour of mustard and incense powder, melted with lamb's wool, then put on light sponge pieces, and do not bind the nose tightly; and if the nostril opening is small, and it is broken into small pieces, if the stitches are comfortable for this, then cut off the fringe, and the treatment of things enchanted charms, and soldering, if like ointments and plasters that are suitable for this; and if there is no wound on the nose, but it cures with tents, and puts on nail-like sponges, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated, there is no wound, and the break is not deep, only slightly so, and it is not broken into pieces, but rather like a nail, if you know how to do it gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right side of the mandible, to place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left side of the mandible, then place your index finger on the left hand, gently press on the break, and hold it with the other hand until it heals.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is divided into two parts, and it comes to your notice that you need to extend the second part equally, then do so.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or break, or there is inflammation, then take a gold or silver thread and sew it around the broken lower jaw, and then double-stitch it; and take a long, wide piece of leather or a piece of cloth that fits the jaw, and sew it to the mouth that you are sewing, and instruct the patient to lie down, and give him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, and if it does not change in three days, then re-fix it to where it was before; and apply a plaster with flour from the mill or wheat flour, after you have osteit the cerote; and apply a lighter plaster on top, and let it dry when it is moist, and the position of the patient does not change, as long as he is healthy; it remains healthy for three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If the abscess is inflamed, then it comes to gangrene, as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, a small piece of bone is broken off in the joint; if the bones are slightly crooked, it can be adjusted.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, let it widen according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all the bones in place, and there is no pain, if the wound is wide, let it be large, and insert emplausteres made of crooked bones as needed, until it is healthy.
