de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The break of the helper
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The helper is the one that is between the upper and lower part of the shoulder blade, and if it breaks, then it must be restored according to one of the following ways:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And lift the head of the shoulder as much as possible, and let it hang over the shoulder blade; then the dislocation is placed on the helper at the top, until it reaches the shoulder, and there is a hook in the helper, then it can hold any weight or extend the arm; then place the hands together to hold the dislocation, as much as the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is if one cuts the patient's hair according to their desire, and holds their hand on their collarbone, then commands the ministers to touch the area where the incision is, and touch the rest of the body lightly, and extend each part to its place.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then tighten the limbs away from the incision, and hold the area where the incision is, and extend each part to its place.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the incision is near the shoulder blade, then it is necessary to make the limbs loose from the elbow, and the other towards the wrist, away from the incision; and if the incision is towards the wrist, then it is necessary to make the limbs loose from the elbow, with little effort, as long as the incision is even with the shoulder blade and the wrist, then make the incision, as you can, and hold it steady until it does not move.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	1. If the arrowhead comes out, if it is not strained for seven days, and it is oiled and greased on both sides, as long as the arrowhead is calmed; then it is extracted, and the manner of extracting it if it is that you place the plaster on the wound, then assemble the arm with the helper, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and stretch the bandage, and extract from the helper and from the arm, if the arm is in its place, nothing will prevent it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	2. If you doubt that the bone does not move, if you use splints, and place the wound with a larger and stronger splint than the others, and have between each splint two spaces of about one and a half fingers, and so make each splint as large as it can pass through the wound; then strain the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly but less by moving them apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	1. If you see the position of the pelvis, and the ligaments, as we have said, in the place where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the incision chaut, if you let it remain for three days, as we have said; then look at each third day the link, that pruritus does not inflame nor the norrissemens come to the member because it is too estrois.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	2. If the adress, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	3. And if no such accidents come, if not the only thing that happens is after three days or more, and sleeps the patient on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and put the assistant in a plain linen bandage, and look at each hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken member does not move, or is not softened by the ligaments; if the adress by the virtue of medicine, and the meat that we have before us, in like manner as the meat is subtle at the beginning; and when it comes to be taken back, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	The patient should have the assistant and leg returned after 40 days, and therefore they must be gently handled and given baths and medicines for the joint to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the restriction is tight and knotted, it should be gently loosened every 4 weeks.
de la brisure du bras	of the arm break
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "ulna," with one being shorter and the other longer; the shorter one is towards the little finger, and the longer one is towards the little toe. Inadvertently, only the short humerus or ulna may break, or both at once.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the thigh bones are broken, the repairs are light and the cures; and when the larger ones are broken, if it is a poor cure, then more injured than when they were broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the thigh bone that is broken, then it will be necessary to extend lightly and put in order.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large thigh bone that is broken, then it will be necessary to strain more strongly; and extend at the wrist, and raise the palm of the hand higher than the other, and the leg must be lowered below the other, and let the pain be on its own side, and the wrist raised above, so that it does not suffer any labor; then extend the remaining members of the arm to the opposite part of the shoulder, or to the elbow, and some other members to the other at the back.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he places it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, he puts each in its place, and if there are no loose teeth that point out of the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then as we have said before, set it and the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken to the individual surgeon; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration, aphthones come out, if he is hung from a cord made of rose oil and waxed beeswax, which is neither too hard nor too soft, and it is hung by a subtle thread, as long as the aphthones are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the osteotomy is performed, and the surgeon places the drill with a large amount of powder from the mill, placing the pins, and making the bridge more complex than others; and it is necessary that there be six pins or braces in more positions: either the bridge is in one of the bones, or in two; and it is drawn more under the bridge than elsewhere, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and the edges that are under the bridge, wet and soft, should not be too hard or rough; and the sutures, which are drawn out, should be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some years.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, as itch does to the member, if you heat the member with hot water, as long as the itch is calmed, then let the member rest in its place.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then the extraction resumes, and if the limb is softened and the bones are exposed, and it seems like something, then it is removed.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not come to the member because it is too tight, as it can be softened by being pounded in a mortar and pestle, and let for some years, until the swelling comes and then it is pulled.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things come to pass in the patient within twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the dislocation is not reduced within thirty years, then the patient can move their arms to their sides, and their shoulders will be equal; they will be still and quiet, and sleep on their back; and it is hoped that this dislocation is restored in thirty or thirty-five years, or by chance in twenty years, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wishes that on the back of the hand and wrist there are few dislocations, and only twisting many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	1. When the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, if the patient can manage to hold it steady, and then place their hand on the extended thigh; then extend the fingers of the broken bones, and place them evenly in the holes, as far as they are well-jointed; then apply plaster and bandages, if necessary, and then place a splint according to the size of the thigh; and finally, wrap it in a drapery made of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	2. If the fracture is near the heel of the foot, then make a ring of bandages, and instruct the patient to tighten it around their broken foot; then wrap it with a long strip, and hold it tightly, as tightly as the heel of the hand, and hold it firmly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the knee, then it comes to pass that you put a splint on and another one in the sole, if the hand is straight and upright, then the leg is held tightly between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes from neither of us, but is bent, if it holds, then as it should; and the strain with the sole, and if you see that you put a splint straight small for raising the fracture, and does not move; and if the fracture is in others, as in the index or one of the others, if it holds, and the leg is held with the healthy one that follows; or you hold them all together, what you can, or you put on an splint, as you can; and be careful in the restoration and the position of the wound, and whatever comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The rib of the patient is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration is if it lies on the lines of the fracture and the other side is dislocated.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient cries out in pain, then extends each of his muscles to his equal part; and it is when the fracture is made in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the rib, then some of the muscles are pulled towards the point of pricking, and the others are pulled away from the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And when it reaches the joint, and therefore, let the ligaments of the joint be loose, and the extension be equal; then place the bone in its natural position with both hands, as it should be, and then put the splint, and the bandage, if necessary, and hold it in place so that it does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has swelled, if you let it rest, then return to your home and your care; the dressing is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the ankle with a bandage doubled in size from I to III, and remove any excess, then bend the leg so that the heel reaches the root of the nail, and tie the long end of the bandage between the calf and the leg, loosening the joint of the knee; then bend the leg and the calf with the bandage, then put the brace on, and place one on the bone of the leg; then place the leather between the leg and the calf to fix the dressing, then begin to tie the third or fourth loops on the brace; and as more loops you have on the brace, and less the tightens; then take out the two ends of the string that you have tied between the leg and the calf, and the three loops that are still on, then go back to the ankle where the string is, until you see the joint; the dressing, if it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, then it will neither swell nor become inflamed.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it leaves, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, if it can be avoided, so be it; and if not, then it must be cut, and the wound treated as we have said, and the cure, no matter how healthy it is.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is the joint broken when one puts it in its place, as we have done with the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration that has been made, it does not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	You should know that the joint is restored in L time, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the right knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	However, in the right knee joint, there is little fracture, but it bruises many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is either a sprain or a puncture, and there is pain at all wounds, and it feels quite bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put the bone back in its place as much as possible, then put the splint, and if you have one, put an iron bandage, and tighten it as it should be, then reward all the dispositions we have said for other fractures, such as apoplexy and other similar accidents; if you put on each accident what is necessary to make it healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "true" by right, not "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and all the mending is like that of the arm, and for this the restoration is done as well as that of the arm properly. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg around in all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bones are broken, then feel great pain and see that it is well; then turn around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	The patient should extend the limb and hold it evenly; however, if the fracture is uneven, and there are more pieces, then the extension should be less severe and lighter; and the bandage according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you have two strips of twisted hair that bend the leg on one side and the other, and are long enough to reach from the knee to the ankle, then wrap them around the leg and tie them tightly, and at this point do not let the leg lean to the left or right, and it is well; and no one has increased the pain in the leg, and it is of fust, and he puts it on the leg to warn against movement, and properly made it there in the fracture or wound; and shake each day the leg to see if it has swelling or any other accident; if the cure is as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot are never broken and must be very hard, and only cracked in certain positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If it happens as if the bone is broken, and you see the bones pressing against each other, if they are so painful on the earth, just like when you are flying, then put your hand on the bone that is dislocated, lift the bones as much as they can be raised in their place; then press them until they feel straight in their sockets; then insert the splint and stitch it up, and make a small tube in the abdomen of the dislocated limb, then draw it out at the knee joint, then wrap the wound with bandages, and other things that you have skill for.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone has not healed, because you will find the bones uneven, broken, displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the two fractures, if they are set, as we have said, you must do with your hand; then put a splint on one end according to the length of the other, and make it slightly larger, then put the peg in the hollow that I mentioned, and tighten it; and if there are two or three, or more, fractures, if you put one on each according to its quantity, wrapped in a single layer of linen, and draw the peg out of the hollow of the other; and make sure the splint is held firmly against the chest of the pelvis, so that it does not slip.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	It is necessary that you do not ignore the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each accident as we have advised.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone break of the shoulder
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the woman's shoulder bone is broken, if it is set in place, then it inclines towards the side of the shoulder, and is held by the arm; then fill the nature of the cloth with the woman's cloth, and put it as large as possible; then bend the woman, and gently bend the shoulder, and then take off the cotton, as soon as it comes into contact with the nature, and return the bone with the cloth; and if she sees blood, if the cotton holds the blood, and if she has bled, she should be reset, and in seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see, take a bucket of cold water, and hang a rope around the neck, and blow all the water into the nature; then let the rope form, as long as the bucket is empty: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it alone for several days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the thigh is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the bone of the hind leg; and these breaks are not hidden that are near to him who puts his study and his use, and he reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means in more directions the right way of restoration: understand the donkeys.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the neck, when it is broken, take an ostrich's gape and bite the neck; then wrap around drapes, and leave it three turns outside, and it will be healthy very quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of injury with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, as the bone of the shoulder or elbow, or seeming, that he be now healthy, if the wounds that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is, if the dislocation of vitrioles, if you have nothing else, then resume to reset the fracture at the same hour, or the next day, if the patient does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the patient does not come the next day, leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the patient is calm and does not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you will have caused an unwanted accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken, it should be reduced gently at the point of discovery, and you should place it lightly in your hands, extended slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not easy to place in your hands, if the splint is this one made of iron, which is seven or eight times as long as the limb, and the width according to the size of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary to pierce three or four times, according to the number of each reduction of the fracture; and it should be strong but not too large, so that it does not cause compression on the member in your hand, and it should also be in front, and large at the end, in this way:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	The first sentence translates to: "And is called 'palisade', because it is necessary that the heads of the bones be placed on the head of the bone; and the bone should be once, as much as it rises, and be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	The second sentence translates to: "And if the fracture is not noticeable, and the strains cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you hold the head of the bone, as much as the strains have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	The third sentence translates to: "And if you do not bring the bone back, as we have said, if you hold it with an instrument that is suitable for your hand, or sharp and thin, then take this which is found in the hard parts and small scratches of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, advise that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you hold it long enough and then wrap it in black vinegar cloth, properly wrapped; and do not put anything on the wound or other place that is greasy, so as not to cause putrefaction and corruption; then apply ointments after resetting the bone, and leave the wound exposed, covering the entire wound with the cloth according to the size of the wound, and make sure the wound does not become tight with the break; and many have had this experience, and have made the patient suffer from the break or rot or corrode never; and the scars are more slick and sooty than the other scars.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, but it cannot be set with splints; then envelop the limb in a cloth, tighten the splints, make them hard, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, and if all that you have applied has helped to heal it, and you use a remedy for painful wounds, such as a tetrafarmacone and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you unbandage the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is not healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limb be aligned in a way that the belly is covered gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they persist, and it cannot be held back but moves away from the belly, and has small pieces of bones, then you must tie the wound with a tent, and pull out all these pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If an abscess comes to the joint, or in any other way of corruption, if you are able to cure it, according to what is written in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, as if it were the bone of the shoulder or the helper's arm, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if you do not touch it because many times it dies but leaves it until it bleeds; by chance, cure the wound after 20 or 30 years, then treat the wound, if you can. And if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of the hot flashes that come by surprise
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come often after the heat of the bath, and at the same time when it is near the joint, and it is a shame to see the member in such a state; and by chance it cannot make the member follow its natural course.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	When the patient is well: if they are given laxative medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and senna, and other similar things, and you do not take any of these, or all together, and mix them with warm wine, or with an abundance of beer, or with honey; and they are taken in purgatives, and the bowels are well strained, and not moved by the hands; and then the purgation is resumed, and another one is begun as soon as the nodulations cease; or if a piece of plaster is strained; for the property of this plaster is that it allays the pain in the nodes, and allays all the swellings in the limbs; and when the nodulation is turned into hardness, as if it were a piercing, and it becomes insensitive to the touch, if the cloth is removed, and the superfluity is cut off; or it is applied to any part of the body, as soon as it is healed, and the cure as soon as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb that is weak after confinement
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	After the fracture of the bone is healed, and weak after the weak limbs and subtle, if there are causes: either because one was too tightly bound, and not as it should have been; or because it got too many knots, and could not come to the nails at the member; or for a multitude of twisting; or for too great movements, not in its time; or because there is little blood in its heart, and it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient sweat and tighten the heart as much as possible without multiplied in it; then give him a bath, and bring joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, if the swelling attracts to the great induration, and the twisting often turns green, as the induration approaches the member; and then restore its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	If the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the dislocated form of the limb is distorted, it is not in its natural state: if one does not believe the folk who say that one must break the bone entirely, and many others have done this in our land; and these bones are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and by chance the death occurs; however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and if they can be raised with hot water, or herbs that soften are cooked, as with blisters of vismalve, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and if I apply a mollifying ointment, as well as it is made, and take the vismalve root, and fry it with lard or sisament oil, and apply it thus; or take fat figs, and fry them with colon fiber, and similar medicines that dry the soaked matter.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the node is not fastened by continuous and long pressure with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement in the limb at every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twist is awakened and made to hurt, as well as the incision, and it is necessary for the bone to be heated, if it comes close to the bone, with a subtle and light cut; and then it should be dressed and studied in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it comes now to bring sense to it.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, if we read it, and by chance if we reset it on the shoulder; because it does not come easily when it is inflamed: many times it comes with pain and other aches; always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier, then I let it, as long as the abscess is sore, then anoint the limb with warm ointment and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each limb as we cured it when it was in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the treatises for the dislocations of the shoulder joints.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are cases where the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocation of both can be in two ways: either they are a small piece of the jawbone, and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and cannot hold saliva in the mouth, nor close the mouth, and wrap the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it can be reset through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If the dislocation is complete and achieved, it must be reset as quickly as possible without force; in such a way that the surgeon marks the shoulder of the patient with his thumb, and puts a little bit of one of his hands on the root of the dislocated mandible to open the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand is deft, to hold it; and orders the patient to soften and move all of the mandibles.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the measurement is equal, as it is in its place in his arm.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is pulled back, then it is the two mandibles together, if the teeth are hot and oily, as long as they are lightly pulled; do not pull too hard on the tooth, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are pulled back properly, and the patient's mouth feels relaxed, if you put soft cloths made of oil and wax on it, then gently pull on the strings; and the patient lies down on his back, and his head is between the knees, if he does not move to the left or right, and does not strain himself, but chews light meat as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws, and then do what you see being done, and do not try to open the mouth with your teeth and tongue, as long as the jaw is well relieved and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset within an hour and are not converted to their original position, then if fever and chills come, and by chance the stomach becomes distended, and by chance vomiting is clear.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a disaster; and many times died those who came, in nine years.
de la forcelle	of force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed from the cost of the continuation of the foot and the other, and it is never unstable at the end, and it is felt well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is if the patient is able to lean on his back and extend his arms; then press the shoulder against your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten; and the part that is towards the elbow cannot be realigned; it is not easy, and if it does not become stable once, then reset it at the shoulder, as we have said; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten, and command the patient to rest until he is healthy; and then again bring the head of the dislocation back to its place when it is released from the shoulder.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder displacement
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder dislocates: either it dislocates at the part of the shoulder socket; or it dislocates at the part of the upper arm; or it dislocates at the part of the elbow, and that is rare; and it does not dislocate from the shoulder blade, nor does it dislocate from the nerves; and more often it dislocates towards the socket, even for those who have little strength, because at this jump it is very painful; for those who have enough strength, it jumps a few times and returns a few times.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men with a hammer or chisel, and the spine of an abscess is shattered, and ensure that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must pull it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when pulled towards the shoulder, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one; you will find a difference manifestly between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hole, and then pull the shoulder towards the head of the shoulder, as if it were a socket; and the patient cannot bring his hand to her eye, nor move any movements; and if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you can manifestly see it at the top; and this way of dislocation is not easy to return, when it is new, or if the patient is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The manner is that the helper gently places their hand on the shoulder of the sick person, then removes your hands from the collar, and gently loosens the joint at the top of the neck; the helper gently places their hand on the neck, extends it upwards, and puts it back in its place, if necessary.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. And if it does not return in this way, then it may be necessary to use a strong minister, and stretch the leg with two hands, or with the other leg that is lying beside; and others use their hand to extend the leg in a similar manner that they loosen their hands from their belts, then they tie the leg with a cord around the ankle; and they also tie the head of the leg with a cord; and they extend both at once, as long as the patient is lifted off the ground once, and holds it steady.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common in IV cases, and if the dislocation returns, it is indeed so.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this does not work, it is necessary to treat the injury. When the tooth dislocates, it is necessary to tie the gum around its healthy side, then tie the ligature at the root of the tooth, and the other end around the angle; then pull the other members towards the angle and force; then apply other measures to the patient's arms, and stretch the large gum of the loose tooth, and extend it over the bony prominence: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is less painful than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	1. And if you do not hold it in this manner as we have said, then it comes to pass that you must press both feet of the maimed man together with a strong lever on the ankles, and on the knees, and so the maimed leg is extended twice as much as the others; then it is hung from the top of a stake, and its two arms are laid on the ground; then command the minister to embrace the head of the chest, and other ministers hang down with the maimed man, who embraces form the chest, for the joint now returns to its place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	2. And when the dislocation is at its worst, if the maimed man has a grip, as we have said in the one who has a tight grip, and draws the limb of the maimed person properly, and also the foot; then put the bandages, the head and the other on, then place the bandage between the maimed person's thighs, so that the form is made; and have it planted with wet drapes on the maimed man, so that he does not bleed, then extend each minister towards him, and the maimed man places his hand evenly in his hand, and holds the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it here. Press as we have said in the gibbosity, and help the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, if it's necessary to extend the affected leg as we have said; and put your hand on the pain of the joint on the other side, then press with the other hand, and pull it towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the front, if it's not possible to extend the affected leg as we have said; and do not lift yourself off the ground, but make sure it is as it was when it was dislocated in front, as we have said earlier on the hips; and put your hand on the joint at the table, and press on the joint as we have said before; and when the leg is extended, it will be equal; then adjust the stirrups, and insert the strap, and hold it with a bridle, if the leg does not move; and rest for three or four hours, then remove the strap, and see if they are equal, if the bridle, as we have said before, and leave it alone until the member is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it should not be pulled to the front, but rather from the sides and downwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee and it does not move towards the knee, it is indicative of dislocation; the restoration of the shoulder is if you place the patient right-side up, extend the leg if possible, and place your back on their head, and place their arm between their legs; then grasp the shoulder with your hands, and stretch the two upper parts of the shoulder as far as it re-ascends to its socket, and the signs are that the knee is gently held in place; then apply plaster, and tighten the leg at the knee, and the bones assemble themselves four or five times, then remove the splint; and do not move the patient's limb too much until they are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not present, if extension is applied firmly, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the toe
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are never used, and never completely fall apart, but are rather bent and twisted.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the limbs are light, and it should be extended gently with one's hands as soon as it is possible only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if you manage to sit the patient right, and hold the ankle with your left hand, then draw the knee towards you, and then on the other side twice, and then pull up the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, by ending and pulling up the foot; if it returns, that's good; but if not, if you repeat the dislocation, because it returns; and if it cannot return, then hold the patient's hip against the ground, and close the knee firmly on the ground between the knees, and draw the leg back so that it does not twist the ankle; then mark the ministers with the knee, and extend the limb to the hands or to the other side; then extend all the ministers equally, and the pulley is either behind the ankle to hold the ankle while you are stretching it; then place the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg on the opposite side, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it arrives at the point, if they apply plaster and stitch up, and the wound forms, and tie off the leg to the thigh, where the tendons are exposed below the ankle joint, so that the tendons do not stretch too much; then leave it for II to III days, and if the tendons relax, then tighten them again at the end of II or IV days; and if it advances to this point, it is a sign of success if it does not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, and it comes to the surface, if you can ease it, as we have said, as soon as it is healthy.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your treatment, if you are skilled and have used it long enough, and if you are pitiful and merciful and slow, do not be rash; and at the beginning of things, use soothing remedies for abscesses, and let the patient hold the hand of God, if you do not see hope for health; and when you see hope, then set the member to the bone, unless the abscess bursts and comes out; and when the members are at the bone, if there is need to use soothing remedies for abscesses and cure the wound, according to what is necessary for simple diseases; and do not enter into a path of despair, according to what I have said, as this is according to your creator, and for the knowledge of your arm and heart.
